"Oh, sons, since I have fulfilled this book for you, which is the last of the science of medicine, and by its completion it has reached its end, and by its explanations and declarations, it seems to me that I complete it for you with this treatise, which concerns the operation with my hand, that is surgery."
For the operation with my hand is despised in our region and in our times has been completely abandoned, so that the science of it has become rare, its traces have disappeared; and nothing remains of it except a few small descriptions in the books of the Ancients, which have changed their hands and have deviated from those errors and hesitations so that they are closed off to their intentions and the strength of it is elongated and weakened.
"And it seems to me that I revive this one with an arrangement of this treatise according to the way of explanation and declaration and abbreviation; and also with forms of cautery tools and other instruments necessary for the work, which is added in the declaration, and by preparation for it, which is necessary."
"However, the reason why there is no good artisan with their hands in our time is because the art of medicine is long and its performer should be well-trained beforehand in the science of anatomy, which contains knowledge of the joints of the limbs and their shapes, conjunction, separation of them; and has the knowledge of bones, nerves, and arteries, their number, arrangement, pulsating veins and quiet ones, and places for their discharge."
"And therefore Hippocrates said that in the name of U is the cause, but little in the work, especially in the art of the hand."
"But we have already said about this at the beginning of this book; for whoever is not knowledgeable about what we have said about anatomy will certainly fall into error and cause many deaths, as I have seen too many times, because some are trained in this science but cast themselves away from it without knowledge or experience."
"For I saw a foolish and inexperienced doctor incise an escrofulous abscess on the neck of a woman and cut some arteries in her neck so that much blood flowed, causing the woman to die suddenly among the masses."
"And I saw another doctor who took upon himself to remove a stone from a man who had fallen into that state, and the stone was large; but he came to him and removed that stone along with a piece of the bladder, so that that man died on the third day."
"And I had already appealed to him to leave it alone, and I saw that because of the size of the stone and the disposition of the illness, I knew for sure that he would die."
"And I saw another doctor who received payment of one ducat from our land for surgery; and he undertook to treat a blacksmith who had a fracture in his hip. And the doctor prepared with his ignorance, removed the fracture on top of the hip bone with pulleys and screws with great force, and did not leave room for respiration."
"And he finally released him according to his desires and removed the splint, and also removed the bandage after some days and commanded that we release the ligature; but he did it in such a way that the hip bone became inflamed, causing damage."
"And I was called to him and prepared to release the ligature, and thus tranquility came about with the alleviation of his pains."
"But nevertheless corruption had already become confirmed in the limb, so that I could not hold it back, and corruption did not cease to wander through the limb until the patient was endangered."
"And I saw another doctor who punctured a cancerous abscess and it became ulcerated after some days, causing the evil to spread throughout its owner."
"The reason for this is that the cancerous ulcer is caused by black bile, which should not be approached with any iron at all, but rather to the limb that suffers from it must be applied what can expel it."
"And therefore, my children, it is necessary for you that the operation with the hand be divided into two parts: some are operations associated with health, and others are works in which there is danger in most situations."
"And I have already explained this throughout all parts of this book where operation is mentioned in which there is error and fear; for it is necessary for you to observe this and leave that alone, so that the foolish do not find a way to speak and dishonor you."
"And therefore take up your arms with solicitude and protection of God, and your illnesses with patience and steadfastness."
"And use the best way by the grace of God to pursue health and successful outcome, leaving behind terrible illnesses with difficult cure; show your arms against what you fear, so that steadfastness in your faith and name may not desert you: for it remains more to your glory, both on earth and in the end, to your sanctity."
"Since I have already said in some of my books:" "No cure an illness unless you know how to do it well, so that you may not be called a bad doctor."
"And I have already divided this book into three chapters."
"Here begins the division of the book, first of the first part." "The first chapter ordered is about the head, regarding the forms of instruments and the irons for cautery, and what is necessary in operation."
"Here begins the second part." "The second chapter, about stitching and perforation, about cupping glasses, splints, and extraction of arrows and similar things, all ordered according to the forms of instruments."
"The third chapter, about reduction and dislocation, and about the cure of torsion and similar things; chapter ordered regarding the head and the forms of instruments."
"It is necessary for me to say what are the effects of that cautery and its harms, and in what condition cautery is prohibited."
"Therefore I say that the discourse about the quality of cautery's benefit and harm is long and verbose, subtle in science, and secretly hidden; many wise men have already spoken about it, and they disagree with each other on this matter, but I will suffice with a little bit of their discourses, fearing lengthiness."
"And therefore I say that cautery is beneficial universally to every condition, both with matter and without matter, except for two conditions which are conditions of the body without matter."
"The complexion being dry and hot, with matter out of harmony; some said that cautery is beneficial for this, while others said the contrary, that cautery is not suitable in illness caused by heat and dryness."
"That person who says the contrary believes that cautery is beneficial in all dry and hot illnesses that occur in humans' bodies."
"And I say, according to what that person said, I have already experienced this many times."
"But it is not necessary to come back to this topic again since it has already been thoroughly explored in the chapter on cautery by recent authors, and considering the diversity of human complexions, the disposition of illnesses in their various places, their causes, accidents, and duration."
"But in other complexions, there is not much doubt, especially regarding hot and humid illnesses, since all physicians agree on these matters and are unanimous in their judgment using cautery for such conditions."
"And know, my son, that the secret of cure by cautery with fire and its benefits are discussed in medical writings on cautery, because fire acts simply, affecting only the member cauterized and not harming other adjacent members unless there is some injury."
"But the action of cautery reaches only those members from which it is drawn away, and if done forcefully, it can bring difficult-to-cure illnesses into those members."
"But fire, due to its purity and goodness of substance, does not do anything but superfluate. And it is already known to us through experiment and the length of service in studying this art that this is true; therefore, I am excused from discussing it at length here. However, if it were not for the fact that my book on this subject has not yet been published, I would reveal to you in this passage, with philosophical demonstration, the secret of how fire operates on bodies and its expulsion of illnesses."
"And know, my son, that they disagree about the time when it is appropriate to perform cautery, and they consider the best time to be in spring."
"And I say that cautery is appropriate at any time because the accidental harm caused by time is outweighed by the benefit gained from cautery. Especially when cautery is performed for pains or necessary pains, sharp and chronic ones, which do not tolerate delay, since greater harm comes from delaying than from a small injury occurring in the meantime."
"And bear this in mind, my son: only the common people and foolish physicians esteem that those illnesses which are cured by cautery have a delayed recovery, considering that consequence."
"And the reason is not as they imagine because cautery is like medicine that alters complexion and dries out humors which are the cause of pain."
"But cautery surpasses medicine in its efficacy and virtue of operation, being great because of its power."
"But it is possible that the illness might return at some point in time, depending on the complexion of the illness, its location, and the virtue of cautery used. It also depends on how much superfluity has accumulated in the body and what nourishment and influences have been received by the person. However, if cautery is applied to an illness that is subtle and affects a member with few superfluities and humors, such as toothache, it is less likely to return."
"And it is commonly said that cautery is the last resort of medicine, and this saying is true; however, people do not understand what they mean by it, as they believe that nothing can be cured profitably with medicine or any other cause besides cautery."
"And the cause is actually the opposite; the intention behind saying that cautery is the last resort of medicine is not because other treatments fail to help but rather because cautery is used at the end when all other remedies have been exhausted, and it is then that cautery proves effective." "And from now on, understand that when I say cautery is the last resort of medicine, it is not in accordance with the intention understood by the common people and many foolish physicians."
"And the ancients said that cautery with gold is better than cautery with iron, and they said this not because of any virtue of gold itself, but only for its equality and subtlety of substance."
"And they said that the place of cautery does not matter, which is not entirely true because I have proved and experienced that this is only true in certain bodies without others, and cautery with gold is good and better than with iron, as they said. However, when you perform cautery with fire using gold, it is not declared to you how much of it is consumed due to the heat of the gold, nor does it prepare itself to receive friction. And if you adjust the ignition on top of it, the gold melts due to the fire, and sometimes pieces of it fall into the fire, causing the artisan inconvenience."
"And for this reason, cautery with iron should be performed more lightly and more precisely to achieve the desired effect."
"And I have already arranged this chapter on cautery according to its chapters and those of the head within its powers, so that you may easily find what you desire from it."
The first chapter
This cauterization confers upon the humidity and frigidity of the servant who suffers from this accident whose two causes are coldness and an abundance of fluent flux, calledorrhea, from the head to the parts of the eyes and ears. It also causes much sleepiness, toothache and stomach pain, and generally all illnesses that come from frigidity, such as paralysis, apoplexy, and similar diseases.
"You should first instruct the patient to undergo a cleansing purge of the head with medicinal laxatives for three or four nights, as required by their condition and age."
"And then tell them to shave their head with a razor. Then have that servant bring the seat between your hands over a cushioned bench and have them place their hands on its surface."
"And then place the razor's edge against the palm of your hand, bringing it up to rest at the base of the patient's nose between their nostrils." "But first, when your middle finger has reached that spot, mark it with a thread and then ignite the olive oil cautery, which is prepared in this way:"
"And then place that over the marked spot with such force that your hand is slowly pushed down, and you turn it."
"And then raise your hand lightly and look at the spot. If you see any bone exposed there, like a grain of barley, then immediately raise your hand. But if not, return your hand with that iron until you see what I have described to you."
"And then take some salt and dissolve it on the spot and leave it for three days."
"And then place a cotton wick dipped in border oil on the wound, leaving it there until the fire's scar is destroyed." "And then dress the wound with tetraformacon ointment until it is healed."
"When the wound remains open, it is better to raise the arm, as this provides better healing."
"They said that the nerve should be cauterized inside the bone, and that the cautery should be held until some part of the bone's marrow is heated."
"And then it should be scraped until the heat reaches the bone, and then it should be treated."
"And others said that when the cautery reaches the bone marrow, it should press hard on the bone until it cracks, and this is the manner of treating small abscesses:" "They believe that from that place, the vapors of the head escape."
"And if the wound remains open for a long time, it should be treated until it is consolidated."
"But I have not seen these two kinds of cauteries done on everyone, only on some people out of fear; and thus, it seems to me, it is better with health when this is done. For the head is opened by the solution of continuity from this manner, just as we have testified in other members, and more so when the head of the sick person is full naturally."
"And the first kind of cautery is safer and better in my opinion, and that is where that work should be done with health."
"Chapter Two"
"On the cautery of the head."
"If chronic and prolonged pain occurs in the whole head of a patient who has long suffered from illness, and despite using various remedies such as plasters, ointments, bandages, and other treatments, there is no improvement, consider if the patient's head was of strong constitution by nature. If this is not the case, cauterize it again with another cautery." "And cauterize that on the horn of their forehead with an ember cautery where the chain breaks off." "Cut the chain and expose the quantity of bone mentioned earlier. Then cauterize it with a cautery at the back of the head where it is called the 'vessel', which is also the location used for applying a cupping glass." "And alleviate your hand in this, do not expose the bone, because the pain caused by this cautery is different from all other cauteries on the head and causes much greater pain."
"And I tell you this cautery in its place, because it is necessary to cauterize the horns of the head and the occupit with a more subtle cautery than that used for cauterizing the middle of the head. This is the form of it."
"Chapter on cauteries."
"On cauterization for non-classical migraine."
"When severe pain occurs in the part of the head or a throbbing pain is felt within it, let it be evacuated with medicines that clear the head. If this does not help, and other treatments are administered without success, then cauterization should be performed in one of two ways: either by cauterizing with an acutely burning medicine or with iron."
"The cautery with burning medicine is performed by taking a dish of salt and grinding it until its ends are ground off from both sides." "And then carefully cut the location of the pain in the temple with a sharp lancet that is just enough to expose the chain without cutting it completely."
"And then press it with a linen cloth moistened with hot water for about three hours. Then remove the salt and bandage the wound with soft cloth for two or three days. Then compress the area again under wet compresses until the wound heals."
"And then cure it with an ointment so that it is healed."
"And if you wish to do this with some burning medicines which I have written about in the second treatise on burning medicines."
"The cautery with iron is performed in this way, and this is its form:"
"And it is called closed nails because the head of it is like the shape of a nail with some curvature, and there is a small prominence in its middle."
"And then place the hot iron on the location of the pain and hold your hand steady so that the heat does not adhere to the arrow. Then slowly move the iron back and forth at moderate speed."
"And if the quantity of iron that adheres to the chain is such that most of it is burned, raise your hand up so that the artery is not burned and does not cause bleeding."
"And then immerse the area in salt water and apply it to the location, leaving it there for three days. Then compress the area with a warm cloth and cure it with an ointment until it is healed."
"If you wish to cauterize the extreme point of the temple according to cautery, be careful not to incise the artery in this type of non-classical migraine."
"Chapter Four."
"On the cauterization of ancient migraines."
"When you treat migraine as we have said in the previous treatment and in the sections on illnesses, and the treatment does not help, sometimes due to the severity of the illness, the first cautery with medicine or fire is not enough. Therefore, you should heat the temple cautery until it is red hot. Then place your hand on the location of the pain for a moment and press it until you incise the artery and cause blood to flow into the mouth."
"However, it is necessary for you to protect the continuation of the jawbone, which is moved during mastication, and that the muscle is not adhered to and that no spasms occur."
"And if it is about the care and caution regarding the flow of blood from the artery that is opened, for there is fear in its opening, especially for those who do not know what they are doing and are not studious and experienced. Leave the operation to someone at the beginning."
"And I bring back to memory the method of stopping accidental bleeding from the artery according to its way, in its proper place in this book."
"If you see this illness that does not improve with this cautery and the patient's constitution is tolerable, cauterize in the middle of the head as we have described, and cure the wound until it is healed."
"If you wish, administer the cautery which we have mentioned in the chapter on the stopping of bleeding with cautery using two tweezers, for this is better cauterization and more effective."
"Chapter Five."
"On the cauterization of ear pains."
"When there is pain in the ear due to friction and it is treated with laxative causes and other treatments that have been mentioned in the division, but the pain persists, then heat the cautery called puncture, of which this is the form:"
"And then puncture around the ignition point, and guide it around the entire ear like a wheel being turned, or make circuits around each one if the pain is in both." "Proceed slowly with the cautery of the rim of the ear little by little, so that you feel the location with caution."
"And if you make dots with the cautery all around the ear and leave it like that, then cure those locations until they are healed."
"Chapter Six."
Burning of the throat
The tumor that is treated and cured by cautery is only of those species that come through the blood vessels, as we have said in the divisions of diseases.
Avoid cautery for the species that arrives dry or due to spasm of the nerve
When you treat that kind of tumor with remedies and purgatives and warm drinks, and your treatment does not bring about healing, then you should cauterize the disease with three cauteries: one at the root of the ear, the second a little below the forehead temple, and the third at the junction of the two lips.
And pause your cautery for the opposite of where the disease started, because softening happens only in the part that appears healed.
And the method of cautery is that you cauterize there with the cautery in the right side of the extreme tip of the ear above a little over the horn of the head, and on the other temple, the length of which should be according to the length of the thumb, and then pause your hand with the cautery until about half of the species of the bone is burned.
And this is the method of cautery, which is a species of the cutlery trade, the form of which is as follows: However, it would be much more subtle if you could see it this way; and sometimes it's necessary to cut away excess thickness.
And afterwards, treat the place with whatever is prescribed until it is healed.

Then cauterize over the mouth of the stomach, and if it is worse, then treat him with what you proceed to do

Chapter X.

Chapter XI
Of cauterization for melancholy.
When the causes of melancholy are corrupted moisture and thick bile, then cauterize it with the cauteries mentioned earlier in paralysis.
If the cause of melancholy is declining superfluity leading to it, and the patient's body is humid, then let them drink what cleanses the brain according to what has been mentioned earlier in the division.
And properly shave the patient's head, and also make a poultice decently from it over the circle, and properly apply that poultice in the middle of the head.
And let the patient be seated, and held down on all sides.
And also apply a liniment; afterwards, it is fitting to bind with wool. And warm that over the fire for gentle heating according to measure, which the said patient endures when it is most in them. And afterwards place that in the middle of the head within the circle, and let it lie there until it cools down.
And do this with the patient once every week, but with the other regimen of the boil until it is healed; or if you wish, cauterize that making little points according to how much of it there is, ensuring that your hand holds a cautery arranged thus: this is a species of cautery which moistens the brain evenly.
And also bind that wound with cloth or gauze.
Chapter XII
On cauterizing descending water in the head
When it has been declared to you that water has begun to descend into the head through the signs which have been mentioned in this division, then begin and give the patient to drink what cleanses the brain of him, and guard him from all humidities.
And let him be subjected to bathing with decoction for several days.
And then order him to raise his head, and cauterize it with a cautery in the middle of the head; and also cauterize that with two cauteries on both temples if it is the beginning of descent of water into both heads, or on one side if it is the beginning of the descent of water into one head.
Cauterize with cauteries all veins and arteries which are below the nape, and let the cauteries be placed at that distance along the line of latitude of the temples.
And guard against fluxes of blood when it is cauterized; and if you see any fluxes of blood, stop them with some medicine which is at your disposal.
And I come with wisdom which is in extraction of arteries and in excision of those, and in caution about fluxes of blood.
And sometimes it is cauterized in the brain between two bones with two cauteries producing copiously.

Cauterize the middle of the head and two spots behind the temples, and two spots behind the ears." Chapter XV
"For cautery of softening of eyelid inflammation."
When the eyelid is softened due to illness or moisture, cauterize that eyelid with this silver cautery device, and this is how it should be done:
"If you must, cauterize above both eyebrows using two small cauteries on each side, avoiding the temples." "And let the length of each cautery be proportional to the thickness of the eyebrow."
"Press the cautery gently against the skin without burning more than a third of the eyelid."
Chapter XVI
"Regarding cauterizing the eyelids when hairs grow inward and pierce the eye."
"When the hairs of the eyelid grow inward and pierce the eye, cauterize them in either of two ways: either with fire or with medicine."
"If cauterizing with fire, instruct the patient beforehand to extend his eyelashes like those that are combed out, until they are lengthened and hardened. And if any hairs emerge during this process, then stretch the eyelids using a bandage so that no harm is caused while waiting for them to grow."
"When the hairs have grown and hardened, then pause the patient's head in a suitable position, and holding the eyelid taut with your thumb, place the cautery upon it. The beginning of the cautery should be shaped like a sickle of iron, placed close to where the hairs begin."
"And then pause cotton dipped in alum or in mucilage of hartshorn on the eye."
"And then ignite the cautery which has this shape:"
"And then cauterize along the shape marked here, little by little, with repeated motions, until the surface of the line resembling a myrtle leaf is entirely consumed."
"The sign of the cure being accomplished is that you see the eyelid of the eye already contracted, and its hairs raised up from the puncture of the eye."
"And then raise your hand and leave it alone for three days. After that, pause a cotton bandage on it until the scar is healed." "And then dress it with ointment until it is healed."
If the eyelid returns to its previous position due to some cause and is softened, then apply the cautery again on that spot as you did initially.
If the eyelids are stuck to the eyelid, then cauterize that area which is elevated to its natural location and swollen, so that the eyelids do not stick together.
If the cautery with medicine is used to burn this area that you command the patient to lift the eyelids which are prolonged and swollen, then a piece of cloth like a mint leaf should be placed nearby.
And take some known soap and live coal on a needle tip, mix them quickly so that it does not cool down, spread this mixture on the cloth shaped like a mint leaf, place it on one or both eyelids, then place cotton wool dipped in egg white on the other eye, and keep the patient's head tilted back.
Place your finger on the medicine and press it lightly, but do not rub it in while the patient feels the bite of the medicine, for the sensation is like fire.
And once the burning sensation is felt, then remove the medicine and wipe it with your finger; when the burning sensation stops, then remove the medicine and wash the eye with water. Then observe if the eyelid has been lifted as it was before, in which case you should cauterize or cut the constriction with fire, for it is now at its best. And if not, place the medicine back on the location where it had not previously adhered until the swelling subsides and your operation is completed and the eye is contracted.
Then place cotton soaked in boric acid or another suitable solution over it until the inflammation of the adhesion is erased, and then dress it with a suitable ointment or another substance until it is healed.
And it is necessary for you to be very diligent in your operation that no medicine falls into the eye, and if the eyelid becomes inflamed over several days and some cause of hairs puncturing the eye occurs, then repeat your medication on that location where the eyelid has become inflamed, just as you did at the beginning, until it is healed.
And this is the method for treating a cataract.
Know that men's eyes are diverse in size and smallness, and therefore your cautery should be done accordingly.
And do not hide the path of correctness from anyone who studies this art.
Chapter XVII
Of cautery for a fistula in the tear duct of the eye.
"When you treat fistula as we have described in the divisions of diseases and your treatment does not succeed, then you must cauterize it in this manner: Command the patient to place their head on your thigh, and hold their head steady with one hand between their teeth so that they are neither moved nor agitated by their own head."
"And then place hot wax or pitch plaster on the wound on the head."
"Furthermore, this is the form of the cautery you will use:"
"The cautery should be hollow, like a reed or a vulture's feather tip, at the end of which you will perform the cautery."
"Furthermore, if you wish, it may also penetrate into the other extremity." "And if you want, let it be like this: as if tending."
"But truly, that which is hollow is better for your task."
Approximately press the fistula if it is open, and draw out its pus and dry it. If it is not open, then tear it open and extract the pus from it.
Then press the cautery which has been well ignited onto it and hold it there for a moment, but not too long at the end of the nose so that you do not burn your hand or disturb the patient, and then immediately place the cautery in the ashes and extinguish it.
And if at the beginning of your cautery you perceive that it enters into the bone, then that is good. Otherwise, repeat the cautery once or twice more if necessary; and leave it thus for three days, and again press on that spot with a border and around it with a drying ointment until it is healed.
But if eleven days have passed and it has not healed, then apply a medicine that is sharply corrosive to it until the bone is exposed and scrape it according to what seems appropriate in this chapter.
And there is another way of cauterizing a fistula which some doctors first described: enter the place where the fistula is and open it up, and immediately insert into that opening a very subtle probe whose shape corresponds to its form. Then pour into that as much melted lead as you can hold in your hand with caution so that the patient does not suffer too much so that the melted lead does not reach the wound; and cover the wound of the patient with a bandage dipped in album of egg or water, because lead adheres to the place of the fistula and heals it by marvelous healing.
And if the fistula is healed with what we have said about cautery and treatment, then that is good. Otherwise, it is necessary to administer traction of the nose and reduce the fistula into the body of the nose according to what will come in its proper place.
Chapter XVIII
Of cauterization of the split hoof.
Many times it happens that splits occur in the lips, and more often in the lips of children.
"Therefore, when treating those fissures with what we have mentioned in the divisions and your treatment proves ineffective, then apply a small cautery knife in this manner which is shown."
"And it should be curved according to the subtlety of a needle."
"Then pause your hand carefully in those fissures until the cautery reaches the front of the fissure."
"And then cure that wound until it is healed."
"Chapter XIX."
"On the cauterization of a fistula in the mouth."
"When an aposteme forms on the uvula or palate or roots of teeth, and it bursts and is cleaned out, and then breaks open again, and a fistula forms, if you cure it but the cure does not take effect, then it is necessary to cauterize it according to the amount that has been received in the fistula. Then put that hot iron into the mouth of the fistula, keeping your hand inside until the hot iron reaches the front of it. Repeat this process once or twice more; and then cure it with what we have said about curing until it is healed."
"And if the wound heals and is sound, that is good. But if not, then it is necessary to uncover the place and remove the rotten bone according to what is written in its chapter."
"Chapter XX."
"On the cauterization of teeth and the softening of gum boils."
When gums are softened by moisture and teeth are painful, and you treat them with medicines without success, then place the patient's head on the table, and immediately apply the cautery of this form: thus you will place the tweezers over the tooth and quickly insert the ignited cautery into that area, keeping your hand a little withdrawn so that the patient feels the heat of the fire reaching the root of the tooth.
And immediately remove your hand, and repeat the application of the cautery several times according to what you desire.
Then have the patient rinse their mouth with salt water and keep it in for an hour, then spit it out, because the painful tooth will be solidified, the softened gum tightened, and the harmful moisture dried up.
Chapter XXI
On the cauterization of toothache.
When toothache is caused by coldness, or there's decay in the teeth, and medicine does not relieve it, then cauterization in that area may be done in two ways: either with a hot iron from cattle dung, or with fire.
To cauterize with a hot iron from cattle dung: Take some cattle dung, roll it into the shape of an iron ball, and place it on the glowing end of the tongs. Then quickly wrap that end in cotton cloth, and apply it to the painful tooth, pressing firmly until it becomes cold again.
"And then repeat this several times until the power of fire reaches the root of the teeth."
"And if you wish, soak some wool or cotton in the border of the powder above and place it on the painful tooth, then place a heated iron on top until the iron reaches the point of the concavity of the tooth."
"However, you should wait until the coal or iron is hot enough before cauterizing with fire. Make sure it has reached the center and that its heat does not reach the patient's mouth."
"And then heat the cautery iron to its proper shape and place it on the tooth with your hand until it cools down. Do this several times, once or twice a day, until the pain disappears."
"And it is necessary that after this cauterization, the patient should rinse his mouth well and hold it closed for an hour. Then he should spit it out; and this is the form of cauterization."
"And cauterize with whatever you wish according to what seems best to you."
"And this is the shape of the cannula:"
Chapter 22
On the cauterization of exstrophic defects
"When exstrophic defects are caused by friction and fluids that do not heal well with medicines and you wish to promote digestion of those, then heat the cautery iron to its proper shape, which is as follows: it should have two openings at its ends so that smoke can come out through one opening while the other remains closed. Place the heated cautery on the exstrophe once or twice until it reaches the point of the defect."
"And if the exstrophe is small, then place the cautery accordingly, according to its size. Then leave it alone for three days and place it on the edge of the wound, pressing it down until what the fire has burned is healed."
"And then treat it with ointments and dressings until it is healed."

"When humidity reaches the lung canal, especially when it's accompanied by cold weather, first, the patient should be given laxative medicines and then cauterize that area with a hot iron in the depressed place."
"And make sure that you do not burn through to the gut or scorch the spine, but only lightly cauterize it."
Burn that area with another cautery at the junction of the neck on the last cervical vertebra. Then apply the cautery to it in the same manner as before.
And afterwards dress that wound as is said above until it is healed

And if you wish, let your cautery be puncture cautery with the cautery called punctum, of which the form is described above in the punctuation for earache.
And let them be punctured thus, and afterwards dress that wound with what is said above until it is healed

"Chapter 26."
"On cauterizing the stomach."
"When there is heat and much humidity in the stomach that causes it to swell beyond its normal size, and if you continue with the same methods of treatment without improvement, then it is necessary for the patient to sit upright on their bed or chair, extend their hands and feet, and cauterize them thus: one cautery on the left side of the pit of the stomach, as long as a finger with a blunt cautery; and two cauteries on each side of this cautery, so that it forms a triangular figure. Do not allow those that are not well-adjusted to cause burning."
"And the depth of the cautery should be equal to two-thirds the thickness of the thigh."
"And the figure of the cautery should be according to this form without addition. And if you wish, cauterize with a large cautery in the middle of the stomach according to this form; and this is one cautery according to the circular form according to this form:"
"And cauterize the stomach puncturing it thus for whoever is afraid of this cautery: You should poke on the stomach with a tent as much as you wish and then cauterize those points with a cautery; and then treat them according to the treatment that has been previously mentioned until they are healed."
"Chapter 27."
"On cauterizing an inflamed liver."
"When there is pain in the liver due to coldness or humidity or excessive windiness that causes it to be thrown out of its normal condition by an excess exit, and if this condition is treated with what has been said and does not improve, then it is necessary for the patient to sit upright on their neck, and poke three cauteries according to this form and size onto the liver on the left side of the hypochondrium where a man lies when he is decubitus."
"And the space between each cautery should be according to the thickness of a finger, and the cauteries should be as long as the right hand's middle finger."
"And do not press too hard with the cautery."
"And the amount of cautery that is necessary should be equal to the width of the middle of the thigh and not any more than this. And if the condition persists, then place the patient on their hands and knees. If they are standing, then have them sit down with their arms extended, elevate their elbows."
"And it may be possible for you to cauterize these cauteries with a knife cautery if you have subtlety and prudence in the art."
"And be careful not to proceed too quickly with the cautery, and cauterize only one third of the thigh at a time so that the entire body may be cauterized and it may reach the vessels. For here the flesh is thin."
"Chapter 28."
"Regarding the cauterization of a liver abscess."
"If you ever find an abscess in the liver and want to know if that abscess is within the liver's flesh or its capsule, then know that if it is within the liver's flesh, the patient will have more severe pain and tenderness."
"And if it is in the capsule of the liver, there may be intense pain, sometimes even tiring out the doctors treating him."
"Therefore, it is necessary for the patient to lie face up on their neck; then carefully feel for the location of the abscess with your fingertips; and also prepare the cautery instrument which resembles rags, whose form has been described in the previous page." "And cauterize it with that cautery until the entire chain is charred, until it reaches the gallbladder, until it burns clean."
"Also treat any other nearby abscesses to ensure they are healed as well."
"And note that this method of cautery should only be used by those who have studied medicine extensively and have experienced treating many illnesses. Although some may have tried it a few times, it is better left to the discretion of those who know what they are doing."
"Chapter XXIX."
"On the cautery of pleurisy."
"The ancient cauteries for pleurisy were made in this manner, according to Aristole: Take a dry, long stick of reed, cut it in half lengthwise so that it is as thick as your finger."
"And then dip it in oil and heat it over the fire, and cauterize with this cautery at the spot between the continuation of the collarbone and the neck; and also cauterize with two small cauteries slightly inclined towards the left side of the beard, and two cauteries inclining between the fifth rib and the seventh rib, slightly sloping backwards; and another cautery in the middle of the chest; and one on the stomach, and three cauteries at the back parts; and one cautery between the two shoulders, and two cauteries on both sides of the chest."
"And do not grasp the cautery with your hand, but rather hold it at its midpoint during the procedure."
"And the ancient masters said that men who use an iron cautery like a rod should heat it in that place between the ribs until it reaches the abscess and burns it clean, as we have described for the liver abscess."
"But in this procedure with cautery, there is nothing to fear, because even if it happens that someone dies right away, it occurs in the location of the fistula which was not healing."
"Chapter XXX."
"On the cautery of the womb."
"When you treat the illness of the womb with what we have said about the cure in its division and it does not improve, then perform cautery on it in three ways, all of which are acceptable. One way is to make three or four cauteries along the length of the womb according to the shape of the liver cauteries, whose shape has been previously described."
"And let each cautery be as thick as a finger or slightly more, and the manner of the cautery should be the same as that described for the liver cautery."
"But do not grasp the cautery with your hand, and let the illness be over before the two sides [of the womb]."
"And another way of cauterizing is that you heat the cautery having turned it twice, which causes we have described in the chapter on dislocation of the muscle, and lift up the cord which is towards the womb where the seat of the left-sided illness is located."
"And let your lifting be such that you lift up the cord according to the length of the body, so that cauteries may be made according to the width of the body."
"And then insert the two vertices, heated with hot coal, into that place where with those you penetrate the cord from the other side."
"Then remove the cautery, and thus four cauteries will have been made."
"And if you wish, cauterize with a cautery having three vertices."
"Then treat the cautery because it is possible that it has remained there for too many days, since heat is more effective than other causes in curing."
"Chapter XXXI."
"On cauterizing hydrocele."
"Do not cauterize a hydrocele unless it is inflamed."
"When you treat a hydrocele with the methods of cure that we have described in its division and it does not improve, then you should cauterize it with four cauteries around the scrotum, and one cautery on the stomach, and another cautery on the liver, and another cautery on the womb, and two cauteries between the spine bones of the back, and one cautery on the right side of the thighbone, and another cautery on the stomach." "And let the quantity of the depth of the cautery be proportionate to the thickness of the cord."
"Then leave the cautery buried so that it may heat for a long time."
"And do not remove the illness from the cure right away because of the cautery, since two intentions will thereby be joined together and it will be speedily healed with the help of nature."
"The shape of the cautery with which the belly is cauterized should be like a keyhole as it has been previously described, and that with which the back is cauterized should be like an olive as it has been previously described."
"Chapter XXXII."
"On cauterizing obesity and sciatica."
"When obesity appears in hydrocele and is filled with serous water, then you should cauterize the obesity on the back of the thigh between the ear and little finger bones, raise your hand with the cautery and do not turn it, and then raise your hand again and do not return it entirely, because the serous water will be absorbed."
"It is cauterized in this way: Then make two cauteries on each thigh, and let there be made one cautery on each thigh with the tip of the cutting cautery." "And let the cauteries be made along the length of the thigh: one below the knee and the other below the middle of the thigh; and two cauteries on each thigh."
"Then leave the cautery buried without cure for a long time, so that some water may be absorbed from it."
"And then treat it with those causes which we have mentioned."
"Chapter XXXIII."
"On cauterizing an abdominal tumor."
"When an abdominal tumor is due to heat and humidity that weakens the powers, it is because of the digestive and retentive powers which are in the stomach and bowels, and it is treated with methods of cure but does not improve, then sometimes cauterize it with a large cautery on its own stomach as has been previously described in the cauterization of the stomach, with a circular cautery and four small cauteries around the scrotum, with a cutting cautery like a keyhole; and one cautery on the inflamed area or two cauteries."
"And if the humidities are excessive and the illness tolerates it, then cauterize it over the navel and bowels, and adjust two cauteries firmly on the stomach near the groin, because this is a perfect cure for relief which you will not err in."
"Chapter XXXIV."
"On cauterizing old hemorrhoids."
When such is the nature of old hemorrhoids or one of thick humors or corrupted moisture, and they are cured with what has been said in the division, then cauterize them with three cauteries on the pus left behind of the two small and two triangular ones, and with a cautery above the navel laid across two said ones.
And if you find that the stomach is cold and the food undigested, and the face sometimes pale, then cauterize thereupon with a large cautery according to what has been said; and with one cautery on the liver, and with another cautery on the spleen with a pointed cautery, leaving it there for some time, and afterwards cure the inside which is healed.
Chapter XXXV
Of cauterization of ulcers after their incision.
When you amputate a gangrene, then ignite the cautery that is assembled like a rod. Insert that ignited cauterizer into that gangrenous wound you have cut open, and finally close the wound with your hand before the cautery reaches the opening of the vein from which blood flows.
And do this once or twice, because if there are too many wounds, then cauterize each one separately according to what has been recounted, and then treat those wounds with this ointment before they heal.
And if you cauterize with a large cautery over certain areas, it will leave behind a deeper scar.
Chapter XXXVI
On the cautery of fistulas made naturally in the skin's surface.
When nature does not obey the work we have recommended for it, and the patient is frightened by this, then heal him with cautery.
Therefore, when there is some fistula naturally appearing on the skin's surface that has grown old and corrupted with humors and moistures, then it is proper to probe that with a thin needle, and also know its depth using the aforementioned needle.
Then ignite the cautery which resembles a needle. And then insert that ignited cautery into this fistula, and according to how deep the needle entered.
And repeat with that cautery burning away those corrupt tissues until they are completely consumed, once or twice or three times according to the depth of your need.
And be careful not to burn the nerves or veins; if the fistula extends into the body of the bladder or the intestine, then be careful about all those areas. And do this only when the fistula is in a fleshy location and you believe that it is not penetrating deeply.
And then treat the area until it is healed.
And if the place becomes sealed and the materials are cut off from it, and remains like this for a long time, then know that it is completely healed.
And if the materials are not removed from it, then know that either it is penetrating or there is corruption in its front part, or it may be due to those causes which will be mentioned later.
Chapter XXXVII
Of cautery of warts.
When warts cause pain due to friction or excessive growth, and the patient's condition worsens because of this, then it is necessary to cauterize them with a hot iron over each wart with an iron rod about which there will be mention later.
And make the second cautery smaller by a little bit, so that three cauteries in a line appear and thus they will be more useful in healing.
Chapter XXXIX
Of cautery of the bladder
When the bladder becomes weak and soft due to friction and moistures so that the patient cannot retain urine, then cauterize it in its lower part over the bladder, where the pubic hairs begin, using one cautery on its right side and another on its left.
And let the length of each cautery be according to the amount of the opening of the urethra. And cauterize it with one cautery in its lowest part or with two cauteries if necessary.
And use an iron rod about which there will be mention later for cauterizing.

But already Dioscorides said that when with the horn of a goat the sciatic vein is cauterized, it profits very much for him; and it should be cauterized in this way: take wool and dip it into old oil, and place it between the hole of the knee and between the buttocks.
And then take a dry horn of a goat and burn it with fire until it becomes charcoal, and then place it on the wool and leave it there until it cools down. And continue doing this until you feel the sensation of biting on the ankle and then remove it because the pain will be relieved.
And this manner of cauterization is called cautery of goats.

"Chapter XLVI."
"Of cauterization of twisted bowel."
When pain occurs in certain members due to blows or percussion and persists for a long time without being alleviated by medications, then it is necessary to cauterize with a pointed cautery.
And let the cautery be of appropriate size for each member, according to its magnitude and minuteness, strength and weakness, location of the torsion and intensity of the pain.
Therefore, if it is healed by the first cautery, that is good. But if not, then repeat the cautery; for such pains are often punctured from a nearby member to that one, so that you must succeed in healing those with cauteries until the illness is cured.
Chapter XLVI
Concerning the cauterization of leprosy.
Some lepers have been seen to be helped somewhat by cautery, but rarely if the species of leprosy is caused by the putrefaction of phlegm and melancholy.
And therefore, when you wish to cauterize one who is affected by leprosy, consider if the leprosy is scattered and cure that with what we have said in the division. And if it is not, then fear over the illness, so that corruption does not spread throughout the whole body and entire complexion of the person. Then cauterize that person on the head with five cauteries: one in the middle of the head, another further away from it, even at the end of the hair; two on each of the horns; and one behind, on the nape or occupit.
And finally press your hand on the cauteries a little bit so that they impress slightly into the bone, and remove the scabs from them, so that the expiration of thick vapors may be alleviated thereby. And cauterize over the belly according to what is necessary.
And if the leprosy has already spread over the person and appears manifestly, then you should cauterize that person with those cauteries which we have mentioned for the head; and cauterize over the tip of the nose, and with two cauteries over each cheekbone, and with two cauteries over two shoulder blades of the neck, and with six cauteries over the shoulder blades of the back, and one large one over the shoulder blades near the buttocks, and one over the buttocks, and two over each ankle, and one over each ankle joint, and two over each elbow, and one over each elbow joint, and two over each knee cap, and two over the tendons of the sole of the foot; and cauterize that person over all the joints of those said members and feet, and over each heel of the feet, and over the hollows of the hands.
And beware of the nerves which are on the heel lest you burn those.
Sometimes one is cauterized with a cautery on the bone of the pubis, and another over the mouth of the stomach, and another over the liver.
And know that the more closely you apply cauteries, the greater is the benefit and advantage. And know that the person does not feel pain from the cautery, as they do from their illness, because the body of the affected person is already numb.
And it is necessary that the cauteries be large or small according to the members and joints, as is prescribed for the species of instruments.
"And then treat the burn with powder made from earthworms mixed with honey and the other treatment until it is healed."

"Chapter LII"
"Of cauterization for corrosion."
"Roving corruption eating away at limbs."

Chapter LIII.
Of cauterization of wounds and similar conditions.
Wounds that appear in certain parts of the body due to disease known as "claw," which is a large and deep cause, affecting the flesh, are cauterized in two ways: by fire or by hot water.
But cauterization with fire is done by heating the cautery like a crow's feather pen, made of iron according to its size, depending on the extent of the wound in that part, and it should be very fine.
Then place the heated cautery on the wound and move it around with your hand within the circumference of the wound until the cautery reaches the depth of the wound. Leave it there for three days until it begins to heal and form scabs. Then apply a plaster made of three parts wild mallows mixed with salt to one part, and leave the plaster on it for one night because it will eradicate its roots.
Then treat the area with regenerative flesh balm until it is healed.
And if it does not convert and many wounds appear on the surface of the body, especially on the breasts and thighs, then you should administer cauterization with hot water in that case. Take a quill made of bronze or iron or crow's feather and place it on the wound. Then pour a small amount of hot water into the quill and hold your hand so that the edge of the quill is pressed against the root of the wound, allowing the hot water to flow to the front of the wound's root. Wait for the pain from the hot water for about an hour, then remove it because the wound with its roots will be eradicated.
And do this in those cases and also on any others that may appear anywhere else on the body.
Then treat those wounds after the roots of the wounds have been eradicated with the balms which cause flesh to regenerate.

When trembling occurs due to inflammation of the nerves or fever from cold causes, or other similar causes, then you should cauterize it with four cauteries or five on the vertebrae of the back, placing one cautery between each vertebra; and cauterize also on the foot and on the stomach, using an olive-sized cautery.
And let the trembling subside and hasten the recovery of the feverish illness.

"Chapter 60."

Of incisions and piercings and cuppings and of phlebotomy and of plague boils and of their like.

Chapter one
Concerning the treatment of water that is retained in the heads of children
Know that this illness often happens to children at birth, especially when the midwife squeezes the head of the child without gentleness.
And sometimes it happens for unknown reasons which are not known.
But I have only seen this illness in children, and of all those whom I saw it afflicted, death ensued. Therefore, it appears to me that it is a hopeless condition for them.
And I saw an infant whose head was filled with water, and the child's head remained so swollen that it could not lie on its back due to the size of its head, and more than the moisture increased until death occurred.
And this moisture is either collected between the fontanelle and the bone, or it collects behind the bone over the forehead.
For if the operation is performed in that case where the moisture is between the fontanelle and the bone, and the swelling is small, then you should make an incision in the middle of the head in its width, with a length of two fingers so that the moisture may run out. This is the shape of the spatula:
And therefore, if the moisture has increased more and the swelling is greater, then make two incisions in this manner:
"Should the moisture be left on the bone, the sign is that you will find the corners of the head open and water squeezed out when you compress it with your hand inside." "You should make three incisions in the middle of the head in this manner:"
"Then extract all the moisture from around the incision;
"And there is another method of incision, which takes into account the size of the abscess and the collection of water, for sometimes it may be larger in the occiput, or at the front, or on the right, or on the left; therefore, make the incision where you see the abscess and the accumulation of water, and then proceed according to what is most feasible for you."
"And observe that thou shalt not cut the artery nor cause flows of blood, and let not the illness linger because of that flow of blood with evacuation of humidity."

"And therefore if you feel earache with something that the patient finds with ease, due to seriousness of hearing loss, forcefully alleviate its oppression with ease; and make sure not to damage the nerves of the ear."

Or else take wax, soften it by immersing it in hot water, sprinkle it three times over it and use it; and if sometimes the ear is already inflamed, then you should heat the wax and replace that with other wax which you will wrap in rose oil cerot until the inflammation has been cauterized. And soon cure it until it is healed."
"But if bleeding occurs, then immerse a sponge or cloth in cold water and press it upon the ear, and use the other cure which prevents the flow of blood, which is described in the treatise on distillation."
"Chapter VIII."
"Of the treatment of swelling that occurs in the eyelids."
"Dry up those tears that sometimes gather at the corners of eyes, for sometimes they are dry."
"You must therefore have those animals with hooves or claws, and separate them according to their kinds, and then pause over the places mentioned."
"But if blood flows abundantly, you must cauterize those wounds with a hot, subtle cautery iron."
"And the best cauterization is near the incisions and openings that often return when there remains some cause of their kinds; but when they are burned with fire, those kinds do not return."
"Chapter IX."
"Treatment for swelling that comes to the eyelids."
"Many times, some cause resembling hardness and toughness appears in the eyelids, and therefore it is called swelling."
"And it is an accumulation of thick humidity in the lower eyelid."
Therefore, their operation is that you should now consider if the greatness (i.e., size) appears from beneath the eyelid and is swollen all around. The cause of this is lightness.
Therefore, make an incision along the width, and carefully examine that area all around with ease. Then suspend it with ligatures and cut it off.
And if the wound is large, then you should close it with stitches; and take care of it until it heals.
But if it's small, don't worry because the ointment will heal it and it will scar over.
And if the greatness declines within the eyelid, you should examine the surface inside. Then elevate the eyelid and suspend the greatness with ligatures, without making any further incisions, and press it from all sides. If the eyelid is elongated by incision, do not worry about it.
Also, after making the incision, wash the wound with salt water; and treat the area with something that encourages healing until it is healed.
Chapter X
Of the treatment of inflammation above the eyelid.
Axcirnath is a grayish swelling that occurs in the tissues of the eyelid above, and especially affects children. It worsens wounds and inflames their eyes, causing them to shed tears continuously; they cannot bear the light of the sun because of this.
Therefore, they must keep their faces wet all the time and sleep with their faces down. Their eyelids have swollen eyebrows above them, which are already covered by inflammation, and there is a threat of inflammation in the eye; and when you press on that area with your fingers, you feel inflammation under it.
And there is a way to operate on this condition: have the patient lie down with their head tilted back, and cover them and the area with hot water. Then make a circle around the area according to its size, and place a bandage over it and press with your fingers from all sides until inflammation has gathered in the middle of the circle. Then open up the middle of that moisture with an incision made with a scalpel along its width, making sure the incision is not larger than one made in trepanation.
"First, cover the patient's head so that you can reach their entire spine to achieve the desired arching posture, as in many cases it proceeds through a gap like a white-hare's form."
"Then, remove that cloth which you have wrapped between the patient's thighs and turn it back and forth between your right hand and left until it is dispelled."
"And make sure that nothing gets stuck in the gap, so that with the spatula you do not reach the wound and thus cause harm to them."
"But if it does not appear at the beginning of the gap, then insert a small instrument gently into the gap so that it proceeds arching. And as we have said, remove it thus; and also spread cloths soaked in warm water and wine over the location and strain out those with powders."
"And some people say that they sprinkle salt on it and pause there in the concavity of the gap so that the remainder of that humidity is absorbed."
"And also treat them until they are healed."
"But if an abscess occurs in the location afterwards, then treat it with cataplasms made of Cedar resin so that it heals."
Chapter XI
On methods for examining the wound.
When the eyelids of wounds are swollen due to the growth of hair that has not been removed, they then adhere to the wound and cause diseases such as constant tears and softening of the eyelids and skin which may lead to destruction of the wound, which is called "tactinir" of the wound. It is treated in four ways: either by cauterization with fire; or with an acrid medicine according to what was said earlier in the chapter on cauterization; or it is done by incision and suturing; or by cantharides according to what I will say.
And therefore it is necessary that you stop the disease in its beginning. Also turn back the eyelid of the wound with your left hand, and if it is turned back, well then; but if not, insert a needle into that one in which there is a seam of pus beneath the eyelid, and make the needle pierce with the thread above, and go towards the edge of the eyelid where the hairs grow, near the hairs, and pull out the thread upwards with the eyelid turned back with your hand.
And also open the seam beneath the eyelid where the hairs are attached with a sharp spatula inserted into the lacrimal canal major towards the lacrimal canal minor; and also extract the thread and place it away from the eyelid dusted with fine cotton or cloth, and then sew up the eyelid with a needle in such a way that it resembles the shape of a myrtle leaf.
But nevertheless it is necessary that the figure be according to the quantity of elevation of the eyelid, for this already varies among people, because some require that a large amount be incised from the eyelid according to the quantity by which the eyelid is softened.
And then open with the spatula along the two lines that you have sewn, starting from the lacrimal major towards the lacrimal minor. And if your incision is close to the natural hairs, then it should be as thick as the thickness of a hair strand.
And then place the onion at one of the two corners of the thread, and then cut off all the thread with scissors, and then sew up the two lips with catgut or fine silk thread, wiping away the blood. And make the surplus threads adhere to both eyebrows using some sticky substance if you wish, otherwise don't bother.
"And then leave the stitches of the wound open for three or four days, and then treat it."
"And if you wish, leave the wound open without stitching it up and treat it with hot water that dries out and constrains it, because when the eyelid is lifted due to the sealing of the wound and its adhesion, stitching becomes easier."
"However, in this case, there was concern about the illness, it is a good operation, and there was no fear in him."
"And here is another way to stitch, which is to make cuts on the eyelid like a myrtle leaf and then lift the eyelid with three curved needles arranged in this way:"
"But if this is not possible, hold the needles in place, and then take a needle with thread attached to it and insert it into the middle of the figure. Then insert another thread near the larger lacrimal gland, and the second thread near the smaller lacrimal gland. Adjust these threads evenly, and then raise your hand smoothly while raising the entire chain upon which the stitching is done as we have recommended."
"And then adjust both lips of the wound with stitches, and heal the area that has been stitched."
"But if an abscess occurs after your incision or cut, remove it with cerate and its similar substances, and cauterize."
"And sometimes it happens that the edges of the eyelid become inverted. In this case, you should use the technique we have described for incision, but stitching is usually more artificial."
"Stitching with catgut is done in this way:" "And first you should invert the eyelid and cut the figure underneath as described above. Then, artificially prepare two needles or two slender probes whose length is equal to the length of the eyelid and whose width is less than the width of the palpebral fissure." "And once you have made incisions at both ends where you have the threads."
"Then gently sew each part together over the excess tissue of the eyelid edge with subtle stitches. Tightly tie off the needles at both ends and leave it alone for a few days, as the chain will die from the tightness and fall out on its own."
"But if it is delayed, then break it with scissors, and heal the wound where it has healed."
"Therefore, once it is healed, the eyelid is elevated and the hairs do not touch."
"And this is how you should make two needles according to this method:" "Make sure that the length and width are neither too much nor too little."
Chapter XII
"On raising painful hairs on the eyelid using tweezers when the hair is coarse."
"When the hairs on the eyelid are abnormal, coarse, and painful, you should take a pair of fine tweezers and grasp each hair with great subtlety using cedar oil and lion grease. Then adjust the tips of the tweezers carefully." "And make sure that the length of the threads is about a palm in quantity."
"Then quickly take another fine thread and tie it to one end of the hair if you wish."
"And then grasp the affected hair firmly with your fingers and place it close to the sun so that your work is clearly visible, as this is a delicate and precise operation."
"And then insert the tweezers into the root of the hair that needs to be removed, and quickly penetrate it through the eyelid until you can extract it from above the natural hair."
"And then pull out the hair above and insert another one in its place. Do this with one to three hairs at most."
"And then remove your hand with that hair outside the eyelid along with the natural hair."
"But if the hair is pulled out along with some eyelid tissue and not just the hair, then pull it gently apart from the sides using the thread that you had prepared earlier to ensure that only the hair is removed."
"And then close it with the eyelid tissue using vision to ensure that you remove only the hair and thread, and press gently and close the eyelid. Leave it alone for two or three days until the hair adheres to its original location and grows back."
"And if the hair grows back too quickly, then adjust one of the natural hairs that is longer and lift it with that, or leave it alone until it grows out some distance, and then lift it."
Chapter XIII
"On treating the inflammation that occurs on the eyelid from above."
"When inflammation occurs on the eyelid, it is caused by contraction of the eyelid when it contracts upwards, either to the right or left side, due to poor wound healing, sectioning, or cauterization. This is called 'lepra' and this inflammation can be natural or accidental, occurring from wound healing, sectioning, cauterization, or similar conditions."
"The treatment for this is to open up that consolidation and separate the edges of it. Then apply a piece of clean cloth soaked in warm water to it and tie it securely until it heals."
"And do not use treatments that cause drying or constriction, for if you do so, the inflammation will return worse than before and there will be no healing."
"Use treatments that soften it, such as fenugreek, and soak a cloth in warm water boiled with it or diachon ointment mixed with some oils. Then apply this to the inflammation and treat it with it."
"And the treasure of your treatment is to persevere until there is complete healing according to the form that was present at the beginning."
"And this operation we have described is merely a correction of inflammation that does not return to its original form."
Chapter XIV
"On treating inflammation that occurs on the inner eyelid."
"This inflammation that occurs on the inner eyelid, which is truly called 'alxacrati', can be either natural or accidental."
"However, accidental inflammation is usually caused by injury, incision, cauterization, or similar conditions."
"The treatment for this is to take a needle with a double thread and insert it into the flesh. Then pass it from the left tear duct to the right tear duct so that the thread comes out on both sides of the flesh."
"And then extend the flesh at its edges using the needle and suture it with the needle. Then incise widely with a scalpel." "And then if the eyelid returns to its normal shape, that is good. But if not, take a probe and place it in the opened incision, and use it to turn the eyelid over. Then make two incisions on either side of the inner eyelid."
"And make sure that the ends of the two incisions meet at two angles of the incision you have made so that when they come together, they form a single continuous shape."
"And this shape is called the Greek letter lambda ()."
"And then remove some of the flesh from the sharp edge of the inner side of the eyelid, enough to completely separate the eyelid."
"And then approximate and suture the separated parts with wool thread. Then treat them with the softening medicines and fomentations until they are healed."
"And if inflammation occurs again due to an incision, suture, or cauterization, then make a flat incision over the skin of the eyelid as previously described." "And then separate with a cloth between two lips as we have said."
"In the sum of the sermon on the cure for hernia when it descends or remains, let it run in its operation according to what is prepared in the form of alxacrati, and that is in the form of many diversities."
"And the skilled artisan always prepares in every possible manner that is possible for him to make the figure return to its natural form, or close to it, according to what suits the patient's operation and tools in the best conditions."
"Chapter XV."
"Of adhesion of the eyelid to the conjunctiva or the cornea."
"When this adhesion occurs in many people so that the eyelid is stuck upwards with the eye albumen and hindered from its easy movement and natural functions, then you should insert the tip of a probe under the eyelid and lift it up, or stretch it out with a hook."

"Chapter XVI."

"And in both species it begins from the larger lacrimal, gradually approaching the sight and blocking light and eye movement."

"And so you follow it with the thread until its end."

"And then repeat your operation on it with reason until it is healed."
"The emergence of the carnal lacrimal, if noticed in the eye by great harm, should be suspended with forceps; and cut it from there on one side, and do not extend the incision too much so that you do not cut off tear flow."
"And then distill rose water and fresh honey into the lacrimal until it is healed."
"Chapter XVII."
"Of Incision of a Pterygium and of What is Born from Adherent Carnal in the Eye."
"Sometimes in the eyes of some people, rough carnal is born and it covers the pupil or approaches and presses against the eyelids so that when they close their eyelids are pressed together and assembled like a ballast."

"And your incision should be with that which you cut off those or with the spatula that we have mentioned in the incision of the nail or with small forceps with which it is grasped according to its shape, as appropriate for this chapter."

"Chapter XIX."

"Chapter 20."
"Concerning the reduction of the prominence of the nostril."
"When the nostril becomes prominent in its entirety and there is no apparent injury or diminution, then it is necessary to relieve the condition. "And remove the bandage day and night as we have said."
"And if sometimes the nostril is already reduced, that is good. But if not, then repeat the plaster with the powders and compression and suction cups until it is healed."
"Chapter 21."

"Chapter 22."
"Concerning the treatment of ophthalmia (inflammation of the eye)."

Approach and place the edge of the cloth near the corner of the eye, about the thickness of a thread away from the inner lacrimal lacuna. Then gently press the cloth with your hand in that spot.
Then penetrate into the eye and feel that the cloth has reached the tear duct opening.

Then keep the cloth in place where there is water. Then quickly pull it down once or twice more, and then if the water flows down immediately, the patient's visual acuity will improve immediately, and the cloth will be wet with tears.
Then pause for a moment; then if the water has flowed down, pause once again but this time making sure that the cloth does not get wet.
Then when it's dry and no water flows down, gently remove the cloth with your hand little by little. But those who are of our time pause here, having completed this operation using a thread made of wool.

Then pierce with it the conjunctiva, and do not push your hand too far in, but rather make a pathway for the cloth to enter subtly if necessary.

"Chapter XXIV."
"Of the treatment of flesh eaten by the nose."
"When different kinds of flesh emerge from the nose, connected but with some cause that resembles a scorpion or polyp, this ailment is called 'polypus' due to its resemblance to said fish." "The flesh [of the polyp] is cancerous, decayed, of dark color; yet it is flesh lion-colored not dark."
"Therefore, in that which is in these lion-colored flesh without deceit or cancerous growth, you should remove the ailment with your hands and place it in the sun, cover its nostrils, and pierce its throat there." "And properly cut that at the parts of the body, and also separate what you have grasped with spatula sharp and subtle from one part until you know all flesh has been removed; but if something remains due to some cause where excision is possible, then remove it with one of the sharp instruments easily and skillfully until nothing remains." "But if it is accompanied by blood or an aposteme cauterize it with what is necessary; but if it is of malignant apostemes then cut and cauterize there until it has been severed, cauterized, and all cavities opened."
"And properly let it be placed on the nose close to the incision with vinegar and water or vinegar." "But if the nose is open and moisture proceeds from it into the palate, then you know that it has been healed."
"But if moisture does not penetrate as it should, then you know that there is flesh left in the pus-filled cavities of the nostrils which have not been reached by excision."
"Therefore you should insert fleece into it where there is any thickness, and pack it with packs, pressing between each pack the quantity of a finger or less, and generate warmth and insert one extremity of the fleece into the nostrils with the ray or with some other cause which is possible for it."
"And after that has been done, let him throw his breath into the nostrils until it reaches the canals of the nostrils, and let it be exhaled over the sieve, for many people have seen schoolchildren do this semblance, and it is a light cause for anyone who wishes to do so."
"And properly press the two extremities of the fleece, one extremity which comes out over the nose and the other which remains in the nose, and properly administer a lock of flesh with packs that are on the fleece, and do this until you know that the flesh is already with the packs of the fleece."
"And properly extract the fleece, and press it on the nose near the abstraction of blood once a day, and do this for three days or more until the salve has rotted everything that remains of the flesh."
"And properly at the end of the treatment, place a lead cannula in the nose for several days until it is healed."
"But if you choose a drying cure, use that one."
"And this is the form of the head purging device with which oils and medicines are distilled into the nostrils:"
"It should be made of silver or brass, resembling a small open lantern like a small cauldron, and the mesh similarly."
