"Chapter XXV."
"Of holes made in the extremities of the nose."
Many times a thread appears on the outer edge of the nose, which becomes enlarged and inflamed during certain days when it is considered a bad omen.
Therefore, you should insert that at the beginning of its appearance and remove all of it. Furthermore, pause on the place where cauterization or burning medicine was applied, which is located there.
But if its incision is delayed until it becomes enlarged, then consider whether it is hardened, hard, of dark color and insensitive. In that case, do not touch it with iron for it is a cranky abscess; for many times this abscess was incised with great harm to the person on whom it appeared.
And if the abscess is of lion-like touch and not of dark color, sometimes incision is possible there, so evacuate the illness and incise it without fear, and cure the place with something that dries and constrains until it heals.
Chapter XXVI
Regarding the suture of the nose, lips, and ear when continuity is disrupted by plague or injury.
Know that when disruption of continuity occurs in one of these cartilages (nose, lips, ear), you should not rely on this operation except with skilled hands.
Therefore, when you find such a cause in someone, examine whether it is fresh with its blood. Then join the two lips of the wound with stitches and cure it properly until it heals.
And if the lips of the disrupted continuity are already separated and each is healthy on its own, then you must cut each part from its attachment until bleeding ceases. Then join the two lips with stitches and strain them together. Sprinkle dragon's blood powder and frankincense on it, place a piece of diaphoretic plaster or another consolidating plaster over it, and let it stay for two to three days. Then remove the plaster and replace it. Let it heal by itself until the edges are united, and then cure it with ointment until it is healed.
But the manner of stitching is that you should join the disruption of continuity either with needles as we have recommended for abdominal suturing, or join it with thread as you know how to do.
Chapter XXVII:
"Regarding the extraction of those causes that appear in both lips within the intestines."
"Very often, many men have hard swellings in the inner parts of their lips, resembling kernels of grapes. Some are smaller and others are larger."
"It is necessary that you separate the lips and make an incision on each of those hardnesses wherever they are located. After the extraction, fill the space with a bandage soaked in hot water, wash the area with vinegar, and then apply a medicine that has astringent properties until it heals."
"Chapter XXVIII."
"Regarding the incision of attached flesh in the gums."
"Often, there is a boil above the attached gum which ancient authorities called albulus. Therefore, you should suspend it with forceps or hold it with your fingers and incise it along its root, allowing the pus to flow out freely."
"And afterwards apply a bandage soaked in hot water or other powders having astringent or absorbent properties."
"If that flesh returns, incise it again and cauterize it with a hot iron, for if you cauterize it, it will not return."
"Chapter XXIX."
"Regarding the cause of toothache with iron."
"When the surface of teeth, both deciduous and permanent, as well as the attached gums become rough, reddened, and sometimes blackened or emit a foul odor causing inflammation in the gum tissue, it is because of corruption, and the teeth themselves are loose."
"And therefore you should make an incision between your teeth and grasp the head of the tooth with forceps to extract it. Clean the surface of the teeth where those rough patches appeared, resembling sandpaper, ensuring that there is no other cause for its removal. This procedure is necessary due to blackening or yellowing, and other alterations."
"So if you are not able to perform this procedure at the beginning of the extraction process, then repeat the explanation on another day and again on the second and third days until you achieve your desired result."
"And know that teeth require various types of forceps with different shapes and figures according to the preparation for your operation." "And therefore the forceps used to extract deciduous teeth is different from those used to remove other teeth. You should prepare these various forms of forceps which you will see shortly:"
"Chapter XXX."
"On the extraction of teeth."
"You should carefully examine the tooth causing pain beforehand and during every extraction procedure, for there is no reason why you would need to look at it again after its removal. This is because the extracted tooth is a sublimated substance that serves as an excuse in its extraction."
"But when the pain is so severe that it requires tooth extraction, you must be firmly certain about which tooth is causing the pain. For often, the pain may seem to come from a healthy tooth and you extract it, only for the pain to continue until the actual offending tooth is removed, as we have already seen in operations involving beards."
"So when you are certain about which tooth is causing the pain and know it well, then you should scarify the area around the tooth with a spatula containing some caustic substance to dissolve the gum tissue completely. Then gradually use your fingers or delicate forceps to widen the opening until the tooth becomes loose."
"And then apply forceps with a large mouth and strong grip for good purchase or strong leverage. Grasp the head of the offending tooth firmly between your thumb and index finger so that it does not slip away from you. Then gently pull out the tooth in a straight manner, taking care not to break it or cause unnecessary pain."
"And if it is not forgotten, then take one of those instruments and place it on either side of the tooth with ease and force to facilitate its removal as was done at the beginning."
"But if the tooth is decayed or damaged, then you should fill that cavity with wax and strengthen it using a fine wire tip to prevent it from breaking during your gripping of it with forceps."
"And you should work carefully with your scarification around the entire area of the gum and guard against using too much force so that you do not break or fracture it. Then return to the offending tooth with renewed effort to remove it, for the pain caused by its removal will be greater than the initial pain."
"And beware of doing what many ignorant barbers do in their haste and arrogance regarding tooth extraction, without administering what we have recommended. For often they cause great illnesses upon people which are more difficult to heal than they were to cause. They leave behind root remnants or some of them, or extract teeth with pieces of the jawbone attached, as we have often witnessed."
"And after the extraction, wash out the mouth with warm water or vinegar mixed with salt."
"And if bleeding occurs afterwards, as it often does, then apply some powdered myrrh and sprinkle it over the wound. If this is not sufficient, cauterize."
"The shape of the delicate forceps and tenacula used to grasp the tooth at the beginning should be long in its tip, short in its handle, and thick enough that they do not bend when you use them."
"And they should have such a thick handle that even when you squeeze them with all your might, they will not bend or be shortened at their tips."
"And they should be made of Indian iron, carefully straightened at their tips. The tips of these forceps should have teeth that interlock with each other and grasp firmly when squeezed together. Sometimes the tips are shaped like the beak of a bird called the ciconia (stork), which is broad and has strong grasping power."

When extraction of a tooth that is firmly set requires some cause, then you should place yourself close beside it with your hand for one or two days until the area becomes softened; and then insert a sponge or tenaculum whose ends are assembled like the beak of a bird called ciconia or guanta, in this shape:
The ends of them are made within thus like a file or rasp.

of a triangular tip that is bent or shortened, which should be somewhat thick, and not pointed so as not to be sharp.

But the skilled and subtle craftsman finds suitable instruments for himself according to what is necessary for the operation and various illnesses. For there are certain illnesses about which ancient physicians did not devise or provide appropriate instruments due to their diverse forms.
But if the jawbone or other bones of the mouth are broken or dislocated, it is necessary to carefully examine that area with suitable instruments and forceps for extracting tooth roots, as we have mentioned previously. Here is a gesture that represents this action:

Chapter XXXII
"Concerning the treatment of prominent teeth compared to others."
When teeth are prominent beyond their natural course causing disfigurement, especially in women and venerable old women; therefore you should consider: if the tooth is not close to another tooth, and cannot be straightened or pulled out, then extract it; but if it is attached to another tooth, then cut it with this instrument which resembles a pig's bone, made of Indian steel with an extremely sharp tip.
And make your incision so that in three days you will have cut through the hardness of that tooth without affecting any other teeth.
And if it is an emergent tooth to be filed down, then file it with an Indian steel file which has this shape:
And let it be made entirely of Indian steel and very sharp-pointed; and let it have many small points like those of a file with which the teeth are filed little by little over many days with ease, so that no other tooth is affected or injured. And finally smooth it off at the end and polish it with sharp razors.
And if it is a tooth with one side chipped and irritating the tongue, then you should file down that edge until its roughness is smoothed out and flattened, so that the tongue does not stumble or speech is not impaired.
Chapter 33
Of restoring broken teeth with gold foil or silver wire
When teeth are broken by concussion or extraction due to a blow or fall and the patient cannot eat properly despite your treatment with astringent medicines, then you should restore those that have been damaged using gold foil rather than silver wire, because silver tarnishes quickly and becomes smooth in just a few days, whereas gold never changes.
And let the foil be of such fineness and thinness according to the quantity that can fit between the teeth; and the way to prepare it is to take the foil and fold it double in length between two healthy teeth, then carefully twist the folded foil between one or more broken teeth until the cloth reaches the healthy part on the other side. And then insert the wadding into the beginning of the broken part and gently press with your finger with skill until it is well placed without causing further damage.
And let your pressure be such that you push the foil deep into the roots of the teeth so that it does not slip out.
And then trim the excess ends of the foil with forceps or scissors, and gather those in each place with wax, and hide them under the healthy tooth and the broken tooth so that they do not harm the tongue. And then let it set firmly like mortar.
But if it becomes loose or broken, press it again with more foil in the same manner at all times.
And this is the form of teeth and the method of restoration for two healthy teeth and two broken ones, as shown in these illustrations:
And when one or two teeth return to their proper places after extraction and have been restored as recommended, but still feel loose
Only a skilled and knowledgeable artisan can do this.
And sometimes a bone from an ox is prepared in the shape of a tooth and placed in the space where a tooth is missing, and it is pressed down as described earlier, and it remains there and serves for a long time.
Chapter 34
Of cutting the frenulum that comes on the tongue and obstructs speech
This ligament, which sometimes naturally attaches to the underside of the tongue or is accidentally attached due to a healed wound, can obstruct speech.
And the procedure for this is to open the patient's mouth with their head held back, raise their tongue, and then cut the nerve ligament diagonally until the tongue is freed from its attachment.
But if there is hardness or stiffness in that ligament due to scar tissue from a healed wound, then use tweezers and cut it diagonally until you have completely severed the ligament and released the stiffness.
Be careful not to make a deep incision in the front of the flesh, and cut carefully so as not to cause bleeding.
Then rinse the incision site with warm water or vinegar or fresh water; then apply a linen bandage to the underside of the tongue. This is how the patient should hold their tongue in place at all times to prevent it from healing again later.
But if bleeding occurs, apply a wet cloth soaked in vinegar to the area; but if the bleeding continues, then cauterize the area with a hot iron specifically designed for this purpose. And then treat it with the other causes until it is healed.
Chapter 35
Removal of a ranula from under the tongue
Sometimes, tumors develop beneath the tongue, preventing it from functioning normally and making speech difficult.
The operation involves opening the patient's mouth wide while they face the sun, examining the tumor closely
And if you find it dark or black in color and hard, such that the patient feels no pain thereupon, do not touch it for it is a cancer
And if it appears white and wet, then you should place the cautery on it and cut that thin mucus membrane completely with a scalpel; but if blood appears during the operation, then pause briefly until the bleeding stops before applying the cautery
Then return to your work and complete it until it is healed with care using wine mixed with salt and water; continue treating it with the other cures until it is fully healed
Chapter xxxvi
On the extraction of tumors from the ears and those that are located in the throat, as well as other tumors.
When tumors appear in the throat area, they are usually glandular and consist of adipose tissue that extends outward. These are called "ears," and if you treat them with water as described earlier but they do not heal, then consider whether the tumor is hard, dark colored, and insensitive. If so, do not touch it with an iron instrument.
And if it is red in color and the root is large, then do not touch it with an iron instrument due to the flow of blood. Instead, wait until it matures, and then either extract it or let it break open on its own.
And if it is white in color, hard, and has a thin root, then it should be cut.
And before performing the operation on it, consider whether the tumor has already rested after being cauterized completely or if it has decreased in size. Then perform the surgery early in the morning and with the sun behind you. Hold the patient's head firmly in place, open their mouth wide, and have your assistant press down on the tongue using a fine instrument called a "mouth gag," which is shaped like this:
And it should be made of silver or bronze, thin as possible and sharp as a razor.
Then, with the mouth gag in place and the tumor exposed, make an incision over it using your scalpel. Then grasp the tumor with forceps and hold it firmly in place while you cut away as much of its outer portion as possible. Then, after cutting away some of the connective tissue, make a deeper incision into the tumor using an instrument shaped like this:
Then, after cutting away some of the connective tissue, make a deeper incision into the tumor using an instrument shaped like this: This instrument resembles forceps, but its tips are curved so that the cutting edges of each tip face inward towards one another. It should be made of hardened steel.
"If this tool is not available to you, then cut one using a spatula, the shape of which is as follows: sharp on one side, not sharp on the other."
"And since you have cut one hole, cut the other in this same manner of incision, and then rinse the patient's wounds with warm water"
"But if there is bleeding, rinse with water of decoction of oak bark or myrtle leaves and similar remedies that have astringent properties to stop the bleeding, and then dress the wound once it is healed."
"Sometimes there are other abscesses around the wound, and you should cut those as I have described for the incision of two equal holes."
"And I had already treated a woman with an abscess that had grown in her wound, which tended towards a dark color and little sensation, the wound had already closed, and the woman was breathing with great difficulty, she had already been forbidden to eat or drink water, and she would have died if not for my care over one or two days."
"And the abscess had grown so much that it had sent out two branches through two passages."
"So I inserted a cauterizing tool and left it in one of those openings, and pulled out what I could, then cut off as much as possible from the other passage, and I opened that mouth and compressed her tongue to prevent her from swallowing her own blood."
"And so you removed a large part of it, and only a small amount of blood was flowing from it." "Therefore, it is absolutely necessary to heal that woman immediately. She should start drinking water right away and then promptly take food. Even though the boil was incised many times over a long period, another boil appeared in its place, which continued to spread."
"So I applied a poultice and cauterized the boil on her, then added some more. And promptly, she got up and walked around, not knowing what God had done for her right away."
Chapter XXXVII
Of the incision of a boil when it is swollen
When pus comes out of the boil, and it is swollen and elongated, then it is called perpendicular; but if it is at the start quite thick and round, then it is called a bubo.
But when it is cured with what we have said in the division [of medicine], and your remedy does not help, and especially if sometimes even after cauterization the boil remains hard and subtle, then you should incise that which is rounded and joined together; and if it is of that length, and it is bleeding, of dark color or black, and there is no heat in it, then you should be cautious about incising it, for there is danger over the illness.
And when you find it according to the manner that I have told you of its whiteness and length, then make sure that the illness is gone and press its root with an instrument whose shape matches it exactly, and hold the onion in the new place, and pull it downwards and incise it with one of the instruments mentioned for the incision of boils.
And you should not incise it more than what is appropriate to its natural term without addition, for if you incise too much of it, you will cause it to speak [i.e., cause it to fester or become worse].
And at the time of incision, use what we have recommended for the incision of boils, and treat it afterwards until it is healed.
But if the illness is frightened by the incision of it, then you should use fire in its cauterization without fear, and the manner of cautery on it is not but with hot water, that is to say: you take hold of the head of the boil in your hand, and press its root with the instrument that we have mentioned, and then take some of the water that we have mentioned in the chapter of cauterization, and apply it with that live fire, and pause on that neither thick nor thin, and fill with that the concavity of the instrument whose shape is this:
Let the extremity of its concavity in which the medicine is placed be like the concavity of a spoon, and place the instrument with the medicine on the boil, and let the boil lie on its side so that saliva or mucus from the mouth of that person does not fall into it through the inward medicine, lest some cause for harm come to it.
And then place your hand on the medicine, and squeeze it on the boil for about half an hour until you see that it has become blackened and softened by the bite of the medicine.
And if you wish, take cotton and wrap it around the extremity of the boil, and immerse the cotton in the medicine, and insert the boil with the cotton into a cannula [i.e., a hollow tube] until the cotton adheres to that cannula, and do this many times until you achieve what you want from the cauterization of the boil, and then leave it alone for about three or four days until it dries up and falls off.
And if you need to repeat the medicine, then repeat it, and at the time of cauterization clean around the boil with cotton dipped in border, and remove from around it what is of the medicine, and wash it with hot water, and afterwards treat it with embrocation, and finally guard it until it is healed.
And this kind of treatment is safer than incision and cautery without fear.
Sometimes the boil is cured with something so subtle that it surpasses cautery and incision, for it is treated by sublimation in this manner: take calamus, hyssop, origanum, rue, Arabic scented sage, chamomile, briony, and other similar herbs of this kind, and join together all those causes or some of them in a pan, and immerse them with sour wine, and boil them; and the pan should be well covered with decent clay, and in the middle of the pan there should be a tube, upon which is placed a concave instrument made of silver or brass whose shape is this:
And the extremity should be inserted into the mouth of the boil so that the steam can reach it through the cannula until the boil is completely obscured.
And then repeat this treatment many times until it is dry, and be sure that you do not perform this cure at the beginning of the appearance of abscesses, for it would be too intense on the abscess, and you should not do this but declare the cautery of the boil.
But if this instrument is not at hand, then take a reed and make at its extremity a wad of wool, so that the mouth of the boil is closed because the wadding of wool prevents the steam from burning the mouth.
And this treatment is good for health.
Chapter XXXVI
Concerning the removal of splinters and that which adheres in the throat, and other causes.
Many times there adhere in the throat a fish bone or some other cause.
"Then you should remove that which is visible from them, over which the cat's eye presses, because you press the tongue with an instrument beforehand, so that what is in the throat may be declared to you."
"And that which does not appear and is hidden in the throat, you should make the patient vomit before the food has been digested in the stomach, because very easily the cause annexed to the throat may be forgotten by vomiting; or else let the patient swallow a piece of bread or a mouthful of lettuce leaves or a cup of dry bread; or take a sponge moistened with lemon juice and tie that firmly to the patient's forehead, for when it reaches the place where its thorns are extracted, then they will be forgotten." "And more you should take an eel and boil it with fennel tied on, and let it be within the table and suddenly it is extracted; or else take a jar and suddenly put it in and suddenly pull it out."
"And if those causes which we have mentioned are not forgotten, then use an instrument of lead according to this form:"

"Chapter XXXIX."
"Of the extraction of sanguisuga annexed to the gullet."
"When the sanguisuga is medicated with that which we have said in the division of cure with medicines and it does not confirm itself, then consider the throat of the patient towards the sun, because you should have prepared the tongue of him with the instrument which we have recommended."
"Therefore if you see the sanguisuga, extract it with a hook small or with a subtle gesture appropriately."
"And if it is not possible for you to extract it with that, then take a concave canula and insert it into the throat of the patient, and properly place in the concavity of the canula an iron wire heated, and do this many times (until the sanguisuga is dead and removed from the throat) and keep the patient away from water all day."
"And take a vessel full of warm water and place the mouth of the patient in it, and wash his mouth with that; and do not let any cause or water go through, but rub the water with his hand once again after another hour, because sanguisuga quickly feels the water."
"But if it is not forgotten with what we have recommended, then fumigate the patient with incense or with asafetida through the instrument which we have recommended in the fumigation of the uvula."
"Therefore do this, so that he may be cured."
"And there is another way of operation in fumigation of that (sanguisuga), which is that you take an iron pot in which there are hot coals and the pot covered with a lid in the middle of which there is a hole, and place the extremity of the instrument at that hole; then give the fumigation from above; and make the patient put his mouth at the extremity of the canula, and close his mouth so that the fumigation may not be forgotten until you know that the fumigation has reached the sanguisuga, because sanguisuga will fall quickly."
"And if (the sanguisuga) does not fall, then repeat the fumigation many times, and keep the patient from drinking, and let him eat salted foods and almonds, and do not drink water, and thus it is necessary that with this regimen it may be forgotten."
"And this is the form of the instrument with which sanguisuga is extracted from the throat when it is seen; and it is similar to forceps as you see, except that it has some curvature:" "which is placed in the throat and the extremity of it is like a heron's beak, which is smooth, so that when it takes some cause, it does not let it go."
Captulo XL.
"In this chapter is the sum of the sermon in opening of abscesses and in section of them."
"The abscesses are many species, of many manners, according to how they are remembered of them, each one in this book."
"And they are diverse in perforation and section of them by two manners, of which the one is for the species of abscesses in itself putrefactive; and because of what it takes from humidity."
"And the second manner is proper to the places where they occur in the body, because an abscess that occurs in the head is different from an abscess that occurs in the buttocks; and an abscess in a fleshy place is different from an abscess that occurs in joints; and each one of them has its treatment by operation."
"And more, there are some abscesses which should not be perforated but rather at the maturity of the sanies in those or completion of them."
"So there are other abscesses which should be extracted when they are hard, and not mature according to their completion, such as abscesses that are close to joints, because an abscess when it is close to a joint its being prolonged until it can putrefy what is in its circuit, and very often the ligaments or nerves of that joint are corrupted by it, which causes contraction of that member; or it is an abscess close to a main member, and if you delay the perforation of it until it is fully matured, no harm will come to the main member; or it is close to the buttocks, therefore perforate that not yet matured; and it is not necessary to perforate a hard one with incomplete digestion, but rather that which is close to the buttocks, so that you do not elongate the probe of it into the inner parts of the buttocks and make a fistula, or that it may be made in its term that cannot be healed." "But you should know the hour of the perforation of the abscess, and this is when it is matured."
"And know that it is matured when there is relaxation of the pain and cessation of the fever, and rather the diminution of redness and pulsation, and the sharpness of the head of the abscess, and other signs."
"And because it is necessary that you know the perforation to fall in the place where there is little pus near the abscess and coming from the cure of the prominence."
"And perforation is always made along the length of flesh or skin if abscesses are in the parts of arms or legs and at the elbows, of nerves' tendons, of arteries; and finally in all places where there is no reflection; because those that are reflected use perforation according to that member."
"But when the abscess is in a fleshy place, it is better to leave the perforation of it until its digestion is confirmed according to completion, as we have said; because if you perforate it beforehand, the skin around it will be prolonged and much dirt will accumulate, and often the lips of it will become hardened and its depth."
"But some abscesses are perforated according to the width of flesh or skin due to necessity, or according to what that member requires."
"And it is necessary that you make a small perforation in the case of small abscesses, and a large one with many sections according to the diversity of the size of abscesses."
"And other boils are those which require the chain to be hollowed out and cut when they are made thus that bread is made, as happened in times of plague and swellings."
"And those which are incised in section having three angles; and of these is one that is cut thus like the figure of a fir leaf, like the boils of the lepers."
"And those where round section and moon-like section are administered, resembling them."
"But that one to which it is not done like its superficial boils, for you must perforate it with superficial perforation or flat alone."
"And when the boil is large and has collected much pus, you should perforate it but not worry about extracting all the pus at that time; having extracted some of it one day, then apply a poultice to the boil overnight, and again extract more the next day, doing this many times according to its degree until it is completely opened."
"And especially if the patient is of cold virtue, or a pregnant woman, or a young child, or an elderly person in decay, because many times the animal spirit is resolved with the exit of the pus, and the patient dies easily, and you operate on them."
"Therefore, guard this chapter with great caution, and especially the perforation where you perforate these boils. You must cleanse the wounds and examine whether the boil's wound is little or flat sectioned, then you should apply the poultices of lint or old cotton. And if the boil is large and the fissures of the perforation are many, then you should pause a moment in each draw until they come together."
"And if in the boil a part of the skin is abscissed or has concavity that surrounds it, then you should fill it with old cotton or thread made from linen cloth without moisture; and strengthen it on the third day, and then proceed to heal it with what is needed for dressings until it is healed."
"But if blood flow occurs during your operation, then you should apply water and vinegar in linen cloth, and pause it over the location of the bloody flow many times."
"But if the bleeding persists, then you should apply remedies and dressings and powders which are recommended in many places of this book and division."
"But if it is wintertime and the boil is located in many nerves, then you should apply powders made of hot wine and oil, and pause them over those locations."
"And if it is summertime and the locations are fleshy, then you should pause powders mixed with water and oil or with wine and oil, and all of this should be done until the third day, as we have said. And then you should drain the boil and cleanse it and apply to its dressing what is appropriate for it until it is healed."
"And this is what is necessary for the knowledge of the treatment of boils universally, but according to the way of distinction, I have already said how each boil should be treated specifically in its own chapter."
"Chapter 41."
"Of the Incision of Boils which arise on the Neck."
"On the neck there are small boils, and they are like species of knots which contain tunics that are made from them; and their species are many."
"And among them are pimples, and those that contain moisture similar to lime." "And those that contain moisture like dust, akin to them; and those that are stony, hard."
"And in the section of all, and in the extraction of these there is no fear, since their extraction does not cause any damage."
"And the operation in section of those is that you express them with an instrument whose shape appears as follows, which is called 'entromes', until you know what it contains."
"But if that which it contains is moisture, then cut it open along its length with a surface incision in this form:"
"And begin at the section of line B-E, then proceed to line G-D. Once the moisture is evacuated, then remove that which contains that moisture, and do not leave it any cause of pain, for wounded parts quickly return if there remains any cause."
"And if possible, immerse it in Egyptian gum, and if not available, in water and salt. Fill it with that and leave it for another day, for with that you will corrode all that remains of that skin."
"And if necessary, repeat the application of Egyptian gum on that part a second and third time, until you are confident that there remains no cause for that skin to heal. Then dress the wound with ointment until it is healed."
"And if an abscess contains hard knots, then cut into it according to this shape:" "With a section having the form of a cross, and make incisions between the two lips of the section and scrape it from all sides, and use your strength to extract the tunic which contains that."

"Chapter 50"
"Of the Treatment of Dropsy."
"We have already discussed, in our division, the varieties of watery dropsy and their symptoms, as well as treatments for them using medications."
"And that which is treated with iron is only the species of hydrops alone, and it is not appropriate to approach with iron the species of tympanitic dropsy or the species of hypochondriac dropsy, for these are fatal."
"And when you have treated this tympanitic dropsy species with medications and find that your treatment is ineffective, then consider whether the patient has already reached debility from it, or if there is another kind of dropsy present, such as in cases of coughing or abdominal distension and similar ones. Then be careful not to treat it with iron, for fear of harm."
"But if the patient has an abundance of strength and there is no other illness present besides simple dropsy, neither infantile nor senile, then the manner of its operation is as follows: elevate the patient between your hands, and have the assistant press the patient's abdomen with his hand, pressing out water from it near the navel, and then take a pointed spatula in this form:"
"It should be long and pointed at both ends like a spatula; however, it should also have some shortness little by little, so that during the operation with it you do not pass into the bowel and thus damage it."
"And then consider whether the dropsy is generated from the bowels, for if it is, then you should make your incision along with the navel by three digits' breadth towards the sides, on the right side above the pubis."
"But if the dropsy is caused by an illness of the liver, then your incision should be on the left side of the navel by three digits."
"And if its cause is from the spleen, then your incision should be on the left side."
"And do not make your incision over the side where you want to draw off the fluid, so that it does not run back to that spot."
"And then perforate the entire cord with the instrument and enter through that incision. Then elevate your hand with the spatula between the cord and the syphon, and draw it out; and if there is a quantity of one fingernail or less."
"And then pierce the syphon within until the spatula reaches the desired spot, and this is where the water is located." "And then remove that one (the cord) and insert an instrument of which this is the form:" "And it is similar to a thin silver cannula. It is made of silver or brass or lion's hide, and at its lower end there is a small hole, and on its sides there are three holes: two on one side and one on the other. And its tip is cut obliquely like a feather quill."
"And at its upper end there is a ring, for when the instrument reaches the water, then that water will immediately rush out onto the instrument. Therefore, be careful not to evacuate too much water at once, because if you do so more than necessary at that time, either the patient may die from dissolution of his vital spirit, or he may become unconscious and approach death."
"But evacuate according to the quantity of his strength, and also consider the disposition of the illness, the strength of his pulse, and his general condition."
"And then remove the instrument and retain the water that is drawn off, because immediately it will be retained by the cord which retains the hole that is above the syphon, of which you should pierce it in this manner."
"And then repeat the procedure on another day if the patient tolerates it, and draw off a small quantity of water. And do this for several days in succession out of fear that there might remain only a little water."
"But if you are afraid of harming the patient and draw off too much water, then treat him with a burial in hot sand, and give him a bath with plenty of salt, and expose him to the sun for a long time. And also treat him with drying medicines until he is healed."
"And cauterize the stomach, spleen, and liver near the site of water removal, as I have described previously in this book."

"But if the time is prolonged with this, an adjusted fissure occurs in the scrotum through which the bowel enters the scrotum; and this happens because of the extension of the scrotum which is in the veins as we have said, which causes the scrotum to be softened, and the place becomes abscessed and inflamed."
"And the treatment for this is with caustic as it is preceded by its narrative."
"And sometimes it is cured with iron in this manner: that the patient lies on his back between two pillows, and immediately cuts off the swollen area of the ruptured abscesses inflamed by section through the width of three fingers."
"And then strengthen the scrotum with cold water that is below the neck until it is exposed."
"Then take a piece of cloth and place it over the inflamed area of the scrotum, and press it against the front of the abdomen."
"And then cut off both inflated areas at the end of the scrotum's vein, and adjust them with stitching one to the other."
"And then extract the end of the vein, and do not insert anything into the scrotum at all, nor extend it, nor any other cause such as you may know in the treatment of intestinal hernia."
"And then cure it with the treatment of wounds, and when you incise the skin, cleanse it and restore the wound until it is consolidated; for the scrotum is contracted and the swelling of rupture is not adjusted."
"And caustic is better in this location, because it is closer to health."
"Chapter lxviii."
"On the softening of the neck of the testes."
"Often in some men, the chain of the testicles is softened because the flesh between them is softened. It is said that this is the cause."
"Therefore it is necessary for the one who seeks care to make the patient lie down on their side, and cut away all the softened chain above the natural one; then immediately join the lips with stitches."
"And if desired, first excise the excess of the softened chain with three or four stitches and firm suture."
"Then cut between the sutures, and afterwards cure it with treatment for other sores until it heals and the skin falls off."
"Chapter LXIX."
"Of castration."
"Know that castration is condemned in our law, but for the sake of knowledge it is permissible for me to remember this in this book; and it is not necessary to remember it except for two methods, one of which is so that this may be known by the science of medicine when it happens, how the treatment of it should be performed; and the other method is because we often have need of castration in other beasts for our own profit through them, as with dogs, goats, pigs, and similar beasts."
"And therefore I say that castration is performed in two ways: either by tearing or by cutting with an incision."
"But in the one which is performed by tearing, the manner of performing it is that we seize the beast in cold water until its testicles are softened and relaxed and hanging." "And then take them with your hand so that they are resolved and do not appear loose from the touch."
"But in castration performed by incision and cutting, it is necessary that you hold the beast and press the cord of its testicles with your left hand."
"And then cut the suspensory ligament, and make an incision above each one with a single cut so that two openings are produced."
"And then cut those that appear protruding." "And do not touch the scrotum with any instrument, but only use the sharp scalpel which is on the vessels."
"And this manner of castration by tearing is better because it leaves no cause for the testicles so that the beast desires copulation."
"And then dress the wound so that it heals."
Chapter LXX
Of the treatment of Hermaphrodism.
"Hermaphrodism in men occurs in two ways: one is when it appears in what should be the space between the testicles, where there are two testicles that resemble a vulva with skin at their base."
"And sometimes urine flows from where it should be the cord of the testicles."
"But in women, it is one type: that is when the vulva over the pubis resembles two testicles of a man, somewhat diminished at their connection to the fornix like the penis of a man and two testicles."
"And its treatment is of three types: two for men and one for women." "And it is necessary that you make an incision in those attached flesh where the opening appears and then dress it with the dressing of other wounds."
"And in the second type of men where urine flows from where it should be the cord of the testicles, there is no cure nor operation for it."
Chapter XXII.
Of Lentigo and protruding flesh due to causes of women.
"Freckles are naturally attached and appear as raised spots, which are caused by gazing too much and observing carefully. And sometimes they are larger in some women to the extent that they are spread out like those of men and even enter into copulation."
Therefore, it is necessary that you grasp the excessiveness of freckles with your hand or with an ointment and cut them.
"And do not finish cutting off completely, especially on the surface of the skin, so that bleeding does not occur."
"And then dress it with the dressing for wounds so that it heals."
"But flesh that is born is flesh that grows in the horrorific of the mother until it fills that space, and usually appears at the fornix according to its resemblance to excrement (and for this reason some people first called it excremental disease); therefore, we should cut it like we cut freckles and dress it so that it heals."
Chapter LXXII.
Of the treatment of hemorrhoids.
"Hemorrhoids are when the vulva is not perforated or when it has a small opening." "And they can be either natural or accidental."
"Accidental hemorrhoids are caused by previous illness and are made either by attached flesh that is born or by a thin scalp or thick skin."
"And they are formed either on the surface of the mother's pudendum, or on its sides, or above it, or below it, and prevent copulation and pregnancy and childbirth, and usually prevent menstruation."
"And the diagnosis of hemorrhoids is made by observation of the vulva if the opening is visible, but if not, you should examine it with your fingers or with a speculum."
"But if the opening is due to a thin scalp and appears between the two lips of the vulva, then you should cut it with scissors."
"And if it is paused on both sides of the pudendal lips, then press your fingers at both sides close to its edges."
"And the woman should be on her back with her buttocks spread wide, and then extend both lips of the vulva with force so that the thin scalp is broken and the opening is uncovered."
"And then take some wool moistened in oil and press it over that place, and leave it there overnight so that the wound does not adhere."
"But if the scalp is thick and coarse, then you should cut it with a broad or sharp scalpel made of myrtle."
"But if the opening is due to attached flesh, then suspend that with an ointment and cut it."
"And use medications that stop bleeding without biting, such as aloes, dragon's blood, and mallow mixed with egg white."
"And then insert a wide lead cannula to prevent the wound from adhering lightly."
"And keep it like that for several days and apply a poultice of dried flaxseed."
"And then dress it with the other dressing for consolidation until it is healed."
"But sometimes it happens that during childbirth other flesh grows naturally in the mother's pudendum, and then you should cut it like this:" "But if this is due to a hard boil in the mother's pudendum, then do not use any iron instrument in any way."
Chapter LXXIII.
Of the treatment of hemorrhoids and tail and red boil that occur in the vulva of women.
"Hemorrhoids are caused by many veins in that area, from which blood flows continuously; and when these hemorrhoids become old and hard, they are called piles."
"Now I have mentioned the types of hemorrhoids and their characteristics, and let me say which ones require treatment and which do not."
"I say that hemorrhoids and piles, when they are in the front of the anus and cannot be felt, there is no need for treatment with iron."
"But those which are at the opening of the anus and can be felt, are those that require treatment."
"And it is necessary to put the woman in a warm bath and then extend her anus with tweezers or rough cloth, and incise those with the scissors."
"And then sprinkle over them the flows of blood from one of the incised veins without biting it, such as cinnamon and similar to that."
"And then let her rest on her back for an hour, and then immerse her in warm water."
"And if the bleeding persists, then make her drink a decoction of sumac and buckthorn and oak bark and similar things."
"And also take barley flour and mix it with honey and vinegar and make a plaster with that over her back."
"And if the bleeding is stopped, then it is good. And if not, then make it adhere with two compresses, and to the nipples without incision."
"And also take wool and immerse it in juice of coriander or juice of rue or juice of guaiacum with white wine, and make it adhere to the place. And then cure the place with egg white until it is healed."
"And cure it until it is healed."
"Chapter 74."
Of the perforation of a hollow accident in the hand.
Many kinds of accidents happen in the hand, such as cancer and stone apostumes and ulcers and adhesions and serpents and fistulas and hemorrhoids and wounds and other apostumes. "And I have already said these illnesses and their kinds and their signs and their cures in the division."
"But it is necessary that I say in this treatise of cauterization how one does it when it happens in the hand if it is of those apostumes that heal, and if you want to know in what manner the operation is done with iron."
"Therefore you must consider if the pain of the apostume at its beginning is sharp with percussion and swelling and fever, and if it becomes reddened and if it seems to catch on something, then do not cut it with perforation, but cure it with what helps maturation until the sharpness of the accident ceases."
"But then you must make her lie on her back on two pillows; and let her recline on her two sides and adjust her feet toward the foot of the bed a little below the navel, and let her thighs be expanded, and tie her arms away from her breasts, and bind each with cloth appropriately."
"And then the midwife follows on the right side and administers the instrument with which the perforation of the hand is done, whose form will come in those causes that they will do later."
"And it is necessary that when you want to administer this instrument, you put on the wrist of the woman's hand, and only let what enters the hand from the instrument be the wrist of the hand and the sick part." "But if the instrument is larger than the wrist of the hand, then you must put poultices on the texture of the wrist of the hand so that it may be prohibited the entrance of any instrument into the wrist of the hand."
"And it is necessary that you put the point of the instrument on the left side above and that the one administering holds the instrument and turns the point until the perforation of the hand is done."
"And when the exit appears, and it is touched with the hand and is swollen and moist, then you must dry it with a linen cloth."
"And when the healing is evacuated, then you must put in the wound a wool wick immersed in rose oil or green oil with some astringency; and press the bandage on the section of the wrist of the hand."
"And then put on the hand, and on the wound, clean wool immersed in water in which mulberries have been boiled."
"Then let it be cured for two days with this ointment that is convenient until it is healed."
"And sometimes the hand and the wound are washed with water and honey, and sometimes with water in which rose leaves or long pepper has been boiled, and then it returns to the ointment."
"And if the wound is deep in the hand and infected, then you must be prohibited from curing it with iron, having cure of it with what we have said in this division."
"Chapter 75."
"To teach midwives in what manner they should medicate the living babies that come out deformed according to figure."
"It is necessary that the midwife knows at the beginning the figure of a natural childbirth by its signs, and it is that when you see the woman pushing at the openings below and desires to smell the air, and then she is comforted by what is coming out on top of her, and hastens the exit of the baby, then you would know that this birth is according to nature's figure, and the baby exits headfirst, and the second one with its arms or suspended or hanging from the umbilical cord."
"Therefore when you see those signs, then it is necessary that the belly of the baby be pressed so that the embryo comes out gently when it comes out headfirst, and the second one with its arms or suspended or hanging from the umbilical cord, and is cleaned from those superfluities with good cleansing."
"But that which is other than this birth is unnatural and blameworthy, for when the baby comes out on its feet and its body comes out in front of its head and its feet, and one hand or the foot is out, or the head and one hand are out, or the belly is out, and it turns its face up and has similar blameworthy figures."
"It is necessary that the midwife be wise and subtle in all those causes, and guard against error and deception."
"And here we show all figures of those, and what kind they are in those so that it may be signified by this and stood upon."

"And if the hands are not properly returned and the patient dies, then cut them off and remove the remnants of the fetus or tie the body with cloth and remove it evenly, because that will be forgotten."

"But when it is extracted inside the womb, then you must command the patient to squeeze, and make that sneeze with condition, because she will be forgotten if God wishes."
"And if it is not forgotten with what we have recommended, then you must gradually return the fetus inside until you pause it according to its natural figure, because that will be forgotten at that time with easy extraction."
"And if it is prohibited with all that we have recommended, then take some muslin and dissolved gum Arabic, and grind them well in the mortar with good percussion, and immediately line the woman's womb, the lower part of her belly with it." "And immediately make that sit in warm water until she achieves hypothermia."
"And when the parts of it are cleaned, then do fumigation with myrtle and immediately apply compresses to her." "And when she has had fumigation for an hour, then make her sit on a chair and immediately make her sneeze and extend the mouth of it, and remove that, and apply gentle pressure to the lower part of her belly with a compress, because the fetus will be forgotten shortly."

"And if she cannot walk, then make her lie on the bed, and strike her buttocks violently with your hand, and immediately administer remedies that you know and have recommended of mucilages."
"And if childbirth has come, then make her sit on a chair and immediately study the reduction of the hand and twist the fetus according to its natural figure, and make the woman sneeze and command her to press herself until it is forgotten."

And sometimes they come out just like one fetus through natural gentle extraction, and sometimes they come out through non-gentle extraction as we have recommended."

"Chapter 76."
"Of the extraction of the fetus when it is dead."
"When you care for the dead fetus with what we have said in the division of medicine and it has not come out yet, and you wish to use an operation by hand, then it is necessary that you consider if the woman is of sound virtue and not affected by any of the accidents by which she might suffer harm."
"Then it is necessary that the woman be placed on the bed on her back and her head reclined downwards and her buttocks raised."
"And the assistant should hold her from both sides or be lying in the bed to prevent the body from stretching out during the extraction of the fetus."
"And also you should moisten the mouth of the mother with oil and mucilage of marshmallow, fenugreek, and linseed."
"And also the midwife should anoint her hand with those oils and mucilages, and also insert her hand gently into the mother's womb, and also search with her hand for where the hooks will be placed on the fetus."
"And the convenient places for this are: then you should consider if the fetus is prepared to be delivered headfirst, and therefore place the hooks in its heels, or neck, or mouth, or palate, or jaw, or furcula, or nearby the ribs, or below the hypochondria."
If the discharge is over his feet, then in the groin or middle of the back.
And one must have the hook in the right hand and pause its curve in that place which is between the fingers of the left hand, inserting the hand gently and keeping the hook in one of those places we mentioned earlier until reaching the cause of the blockage.
Then pause and place another hook, or the third one if necessary, in such a way that there is attraction equally on all sides, and not only extension according to its own rectitude.
And let it be moved in every part so that the discharge of it is alleviated just as it is done in the extraction of a tooth.
And it is necessary that the extension be softened in water; and if any part of it is retained, then the midwife must grease some of her fingers with oil and insert them carefully and move them around with the water that is retained.
Therefore if the part of the fetus has been expelled, then the hooks must be changed to one that is larger; and do this until the entire fetus has been expelled.
But if the hand is already expelled but cannot be reduced by traction of it, then a cloth should be wrapped around that one and immediately cut it at its junction or at the wrist.
And similarly you must do with the other hand and both feet.
But if the head of the fetus is large or there is difficulty in its expulsion, or it is in a caput fixed position, then one must insert spatulas between those bones and cleave the head and extract the water, or dilate that with an instrument called "alundat" whose form will come along with the forms of the other instruments in the chapter which follows this.
And similarly do if the fetus is naturally large headed: and then you must cut it with an emollient or dilate it with an alundat as we have said; and immediately extract the bones with forceps.
And if the head is expelled but is obstructed by the foramen magnum, then you must cut it until the humidity that is in the pituitary gland is drained out.
But if there is no complication or obstruction to its expulsion, then you must cut the head as much as it is possible for you.
And if the left side of the abdomen is inflamed or it is in a hydrops condition, then you must pierce it until the humidity that is within it is drained out.
But if the fetus is lying on its back, then the traction of it will be easy and directing it towards the mother's vulva will also be easy.
But if it is obstructed near the abdomen and the pituitary gland, then you must extract that with cloth which you will have wrapped around your hand, and then cut the abdomen and the pituitary gland until that water flows out of them.
But if the other members are obstinate and the head returns back, then insert your left hand; but if the mother's vulva is obstructed, then insert your hand into the lower abdomen and encircle the head with it, and pull it towards the mother's vulva, and immediately insert a hook or two hooks and pull it with those.
And if the mother's vulva is obstructed by a hard clots of blood which has accumulated there, then you must not rub it over it. Rather, you must administer an injection of hot water to dissolve the thick and fatty causes. And apply plasters; and follow up with the patient in waters that soften and moisturize.
And if the fetus is lying on its side, then if it is possible, you should turn it; and administer to it what we have said for a live fetus.
But if that is not possible, then cut it in pieces and extract it.
And you must not leave any cause behind in the uterus.
And when you have completed your operation, then administer to her what we have said about the treatment of hard clots of blood that may have occurred in the mother.
And if there is bleeding, then apply styptic waters and administer the other treatment.
And I have seen a woman whose uterus contained a dead fetus, and later she became pregnant again, but the second time also the fetus was dead. It happened that for a long time there was a hard clot of blood in her uterus; it became inflamed and started to expel, but the fetus died.
And I was called to treat her for this, and treated her for a long time, but the illness did not improve.
Then I applied to her some plasters with strong attraction, and about three days later she expelled one bone, and after a few more days she expelled another bone. And I was greatly amazed, because there are no bones in the uterus.
And then I thought that they were the bones of the dead fetus.
Therefore I healed her illness and extracted from her many bones, the woman living in good health ever since, except for some slight bleeding.
And I do not affirm that this is strange, but rather it shows the knowledge and skill of the doctor who with his hands administers treatment to cure.
Of the forms of the instruments necessary for extracting the fetus
Form of forceps with which the mother is opened:
This is the form of a forceps in which the tongs are attached to two pieces of wood. However, this forceps must be more slender and made either of iron or brass or boxwood.
And let each piece of wood be two fingers wide and the edge of each one a finger's width apart, and its length one and a half palms; and in the middle of the two pieces of wood there are two joints for fitting together these pieces of wood which are already fastened, and their length is about one and a half palms, and their width two fingers or a little more.
And these two additions are inserted into the mother's vulva so that it is opened with them when you turn the two prescribed forceps.
Another similar form, but more slender and lighter:
Let it be made of brass or boxwood according to the shape of forceps. But instead at its end let there be two additions like this: and the length of each addition is about one palm, and their width two fingers.
And when you want to open the mother with these, then have the woman lie on her back with her feet raised up high, and open what is between the lips of it. And then open your hand with the instrument as you do with forceps attached according to how much you want of the opening of the mother's vulva where you want the uterus to be opened.
The form of forceps described by the ancients:
Form of a probe with which the fetus is pushed:
Form of a hook with which the large head is grasped
And it is like a forceps with teeth at the end like this: and sometimes it is made long like this forceps according to this form, like this: with teeth like those of a rake with which it is inserted and grasps. Form of a small hook:
"A shape having a spine."
"A shape having two spines."
"A spatula having two ends where the head is severed."
"Form of two spatulas lying side by side."
"The more these instruments are exercised, and the more species of them there are prepared by the artisans, the easier their operation becomes, and the greater the number of people they benefit."
"And you should not neglect any of those instruments, for the need for them is not excusable."
"For extracting the afterbirth."
"When the afterbirth is retained at childbirth, you must order the midwife to hold her breath, and then make her sneeze with conditions, and press your hand over her mouth and nose. If it comes out by this means, so much the better."
"And if not, then take a cloth and pierce it with a hole in the middle, and put it over the mother's mouth, having first burned some herbs such as calamint, rue, aneth, chamomile, Arabic scordium, cassia wood, and Saint John's wort." "All these herbs or some of them should be immersed in water in the cloth, and then placed on the fire."
"And immediately place a reed cane into the mother's mouth, and hold it there until the steam comes to the concave part of her."
"And then make her sneeze as we have said, and the afterbirth will be expelled with great speed."
"But if even with this treatment the afterbirth is not expelled, then you should order the midwife to immerse her left hand in olive oil or an emulsion of althea, and then insert it into the womb and search for the afterbirth with that, and when she has found it, take it out little by little. But if it is adherent in the entrance of the mother, then insert your hand as we have recommended, and when you have found the afterbirth, remove it little by little according to rectitude so that the mother does not suffer from violent traction." "It is necessary that they be changed on the right and left sides with ease."
"And if the mother's mouth is obstructed, we have already recommended the treatment with sneezing and the medication of the cloth with herbs."
"But if it is not expelled with all the causes we have recommended, then be sure not to weary yourself in repeated attempts at traction, but rather what has come out from there to the mother's mouth should be placed on the thing of the woman, and then dress that with grease and tetrafarmacon; for that will cause it to rot there after a few days and will be dissolved and expelled."
"But when it has rotted, it causes bad odor to the head and stomach, and that leads to illness. And then fumigations and appropriate remedies should be administered for that."
"But some of the Ancients used fumigation with nasturtiums and dried figs."
"Form of an instrument with which a woman is fumigated due to the retention of menses and afterbirth:"
"It should be made of glass or earthenware."

"On the treatment of the unperforated anus of a child:"
"Many children are born with their anuses unperforated, which are often narrow and closed." "Therefore, it is necessary for the midwife to perforate that closure with her finger; and if not, then perforate it with a sharp spatula, being careful not to touch the intestine."
"And then place over it wool soaked in wine and oil, and treat it with grease until healed."
"But if you fear that it is closed again, then place in the anus a cannula for several days, and remove it when the child wants to defecate."
"And it also happens that the anus becomes closed due to consolidation of a plug or an abscess. Therefore, that consolidation should be incised and then treated with what we have said about treatment and lead."
"On the treatment of fistulas that develop in this place:"
"The fistulas that develop in the lower part of the buttocks are usually hard and thick, which develop near the anus or in the space between the two buttocks."
"And it is one fistula or more."
"And when that hardness has become ancient and corroded by moisture, it is usually accompanied by offensive white pus or subtle putrefaction. And sometimes there are penetrating fistulas in these fistulas."
"And these penetrate through what comes out of them through the exit and through windiness. And sometimes the condition is that of exit, and often worms come out from them."
"And sometimes there are penetrating fistulas in the space that penetrate into the bladder and into the urethra. And these penetrations also occur into the junction of the vulva and into the anus."
"And that which indicates a penetrating fistula into the anus and a non-penetrating one is when you insert your finger into the anus, and when there is not tortuosity, insert a thin probe of earthenware or iron into the fistula."
"But if there is tortuosity in that one, then insert into it a thin probe of lead or horsehair until you feel the probe or the hair on your finger."
"And if you do not feel it at all and there is no evidence of exit or worms or windiness from the anus, as we have said, then know that it is non-penetrating. And then proceed to treatment."
"And when the fistula is penetrating into the bladder or into the urethra, then its sign is the exit of urine from it. And prohibition of it until that place has healed with medicine."
"But if it is penetrating into the vulva or into the bone and accompanied by pain in the area, then its sign is that a probe passed into it here does not have tortuosity. And there is pain in the area of the bone; and there is always putrefaction from it; and no medication is beneficial for it, nor can it be consolidated with grease."
"And in all those penetrating fistulas there is no complete cure. And the treatment of these is difficult and beyond the ability of many physicians."
"But in that which is not penetrating and not ancient, healing with iron is hoped for according to what I will recommend to you, and what I have already said and proven."
"And it is that the condition affects you between your buttocks, mainly over the two bones, elevates the cheeks of the buttocks internally, and inclines the vulva towards its belly. And then insert a probe of lead or earthenware if there is tortuosity in the fistula, until you know where the probe passes."
"And if that condition affects around the anus, then it is necessary for you to insert your finger into the anus."
"And if you feel the probe already penetrating through your finger itself, other than what you feel between your finger and that siphac or flesh, then know for certain that it is penetrating. And do not treat it there, because there is no healing of it, as we have said."
"However, some say that it is beneficial in certain cases."
"For the treatment in which improvement is hoped, you should cauterize with fire subtly according to the width of the fistula, as is described above, and insert that heated metal into the fistula until it reaches around the bone; and repeat this process two or three times until you know that all those flesh tissues surrounding the fistula have been burnt, which resemble a bird's feather quill."
"And then dress that with damp cloths wrapped in wool until all those burnt flesh tissues have healed, and then treat it with medicines that generate and consolidate flesh, and if it has healed, good; but if not, at that time it will not heal with any other treatment."
"And if the probe enters and does not penetrate within the aforementioned opening which is in the anus, and there is between that and the probe a veil of skin or membrane, then close up that fistula so that its surface area matches the thickness of the probe; then cut off the probe at the beginning of the fistula, and you will see it dried with the probe inside the fistula until the section reaches the place where the end of the probe had reached, and through the probe it is freed and removed."
"And then cleanse those flesh tissues that resemble a bird's feather quill with the cautery without breaking any of them due to some cause."
"But if pus starts flowing between you and your operation while dissecting those flesh tissues, then it is good that it should be cauterized with fire or with a sharp instrument, because cauterizing with fire has two advantages: it is an adjustment of those flesh tissues that have adhered, and it is evacuation of the pus, and drying of the moisture."
"And then treat it with damp cloths wrapped in wool or fine linen until the place becomes warm, and at that time treat the wound with soft flesh-generating and consolidating ointments."
"And these are medicines in which astringency and drying are predominant; when the wound has healed, it is restored and there will be no recurrence."
"But if the fistula has already reached the perineum and is elongated from the surface of the skin, then insert the probe into the anus and explore with it."
"And then if the probe meets and there is between it and the veil of skin or membrane an obstruction to penetration, then it is not an operation on that site but rather through trust and hope."
"And there are three ways to deal with this: either cauterize it in the way we have described; or dry it up until it achieves concavity so that you can enter your probes and perform the cure proposed; and do not proceed with cutting lest you injure the contents of the colon, and thus cause discomfort through a surgical intervention without consent. And then treat it with what has been said because it will be healed quickly if done correctly. Or else dissect that veil and clean out that pus which dries up within the anus in the way we have described, either with a probe or with another instrument of sharp point; and then cleanse those fistulous flesh tissues which are in the section through cautery. And then make sure to restore all the wound with cutting, and if the opening above is not consolidated, and the fistula remains open at the partition of the anus, and pus continues to flow from it." "And some fistulas are ended in this way: when you insert the probe into the fistula, and it goes towards the side of the anus around the surface of the skin with the cord and the margin of the anus, then take a probe with a perforated tip, which is like a needle for preparing hearts in this shape:"
"and insert it into that vein wrapped in veins or around those; and then insert the probe with a thread into the fistula until it achieves concavity."
"But if it penetrates into the margin of the anus backwards, then you extract that thread from that tract in such a way that you insert your little finger into the anus; and pull out the end of the thread and tie the two ends together, and burn each one separately, and leave it like that for one or two days. And when you incise the thread in the flesh, burn it well so that those flesh tissues which are between the two ends of the thread and which have been injured may be healed."
"And then treat the wound until it is consolidated and healed."
"But if the opening of the fistula is not penetrating, then make it penetrate in whatever way you are prepared to do so, but do not do it too deeply into the perineum, lest you injure the colon. And then treat it until it is healed."
"The shape of the spatula used to split open the fistula is like this: its curvature is very sharp and the other end is not sharp, so that you do not injure anything unnecessary, as happens sometimes."
"About the suturing of hemorrhoids from which blood flows in the incision of those."
"Hemorrhoids are of two kinds: for some are between the buttocks and resemble coal, or else those which have the appearance of fatty tumors." "And some are small and large, and blood flows from them continuously, and they are singular or multiple, and they are outside the anus or at its extremities."
"But those hemorrhoids that are outside the anus are according to the laws of little moisture, from which yellow water or a little blood flows continuously, and they are according to the color of the body."
"The treatment for those hemorrhoids that are inside the anus is to have the patient sit down and squeeze so that the anus empties out and the hemorrhoids appear to you." "Then you take hold of them with forceps or with your fingers and suspend them, and then incise them at their roots."
"But if the forceps do not hold them because of the moisture and softness of those hemorrhoids, then take them with rough cloth or with cotton or with a wool pad, and extract them with your fingers, and then incise them and sprinkle some powdered myrrh on them at the incision so that they may adhere to them instead of cauterizing; or else cauterize them according to what has been said in the chapter on cauterization." "And then treat those with another cure until they are healed."
"And if the anus does not obey to evacuation, then have the patient rinse with a small rinsing syringe and wash it with water that is in the anus so that it may easily evacuate when the patient squeezes."
"But if the hemorrhoids are outside the anus, then their cause is light, and it is because you take them with your fingernail or with forceps and incise them, and then treat them with what has been said until they are healed."
"And if you make an incision, then you must administer a suture to them in this way: take thread wrapped and insert it into the needle and then extract the hemorrhoids from the parts above and make the thread penetrate with the needle into the root of the other part, and wrap both ends of the thread around the part below the needle, and tie the hemorrhoid tightly, and cut the thread."
"And do this to all of them, and leave one and do not tie it, so that the excess blood may flow from that one."
"And then apply over the anus a cloth dipped in rose oil or cerate, and have the patient rest on their back." "And then let that one enter what box; and when it's closed, care for those with gentleness or with another cure until they are healed."
"And since those remedies are old and do not work in this medicine, you should now use a spatula point or your fingernail to penetrate into the fistulas so that they become humid and then remove the pus on top of them, which prevents consolidation. Then treat them until they are consolidated."
"Now you remove as much pus as possible with the first entrance so that it does not sanctify and they are healed. Then treat them until they are healed."
"Know that haemorrhoids are like keys and if they are not red, they resemble the head of a nail. They occur throughout the body but more so in areas near the buttocks and genitals, where they cause pain."
"And then you should excise what resembles the head of the key with scissors or a nail clipper, and remove it from its root. Then treat it."
"If you wish, cauterize the second one that is precedent in its chapter."
"Verruca is a small, rough, fistulated elevation on the surface of the body, often seen in many children."
"The treatment for it is to stretch and excise that, or shave it with a file or tweezers until it bleeds." "And if you wish, cauterize it with fire or with an acute medicine, as we have said."
"Molluscum is a small, fatty or fistulated elevation on the surface of the body, occurring mostly on the face. When it is rubbed against, it feels like an ant bite and it spreads around the body."
"The treatment for it is to take a quill of an owl or eagle feather and make it strong. Place the feather on the molluscum so that its circle encloses the parts around it. Then rotate your hand with the quill to excise what is around the molluscum, pressing down on the skin, and eradicate the molluscum from its root."

"Regarding the shape of the instruments used for giving Communion."
"Some Communion wafers are made of silver or pewter or melted lead; and sometimes they are made in various sizes according to those who are administering them, for the one used in the care of small children should be small; and those for sick people or the dying, their wafers should also be small."
"The shape of Communion wafers is large and few:"

"And let the bag in which medicines are placed for urinary tract disorders or made from sheep's skin, and its opening should be one palm wide."
"And let it be pierced with many holes as it is rolled up; and the space between the holes should be about the thickness of a finger."
"And appropriate put into those holes strong strings of flax thread which are made of ten threads, or wind them around them; and fasten the bag with that; and when the bag is placed in it, tighten it at the head of the wafer between two distances with strong constriction, and crimp it with that each string: But know that the quality of crimping it is such that you fill the medicine bag which has been heated according to the quantity of the patient's tolerance; and see to it that it is not too hot nor too cold."
"And then the patient should lie on their back and elevate their hips up high, and place beneath them one cover upon which will be the bed or cloth; and appropriate anoint the extremity of the cautery with oil or egg albumen or fenugreek mucilage or similar substances; and appropriate insert it into the anus gently; and then the assistant takes the bag and squeezes it strongly two or three times until all that is in the probe is expelled from the bowel; and then remove the probe, and the patient lifts their hips up against the wall."
"And if the medicine forces that out, hold it until it stops flowing; and if they sleep with it like that all night long, it is better for their recovery."
